Types of Ijma': Qawli and Sukuti
Distinguishing explicit and tacit consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qawli and sukuti ijma' and explain why their authority differs.

Core Idea
Qawli ijma' is binding by consensus; sukuti ijma' is disputed in its validity and conditions.

Ijma' (consensus) is a primary source of Islamic law, but not all consensus carries the same weight. This passage introduces two fundamental types: explicit (qawli) and tacit (sukuti). Understanding their distinction is crucial for evaluating the authority of different scholarly positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Scan the passage and name both types of ijma' mentioned.
2
Define each type
For qawli, note that it involves explicit agreement after discussion. For sukuti, note that it is inferred from silence when a ruling is known.
3
Compare their epistemological status
Recognize that qawli is undisputed (hujjah musallamah), while sukuti is highly contested.
4
Identify the points of dispute over sukuti
According to the passage, the dispute concerns its validity (i'tibar), degree (daraja), and conditions (shurut).
5
Relate to Hanafi position
In the Hanafi school, sukuti ijma' is accepted as hujjah under specific conditions, such as the absence of duress and the ability to object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣/ ٥ - والإجماع نوعان: قولي وسكوتي.
فالقولي يكون بتداول الرأي واتفاق صريح من العلماء.
والسكوتي يكون بأن يفتي أحدهم بحكم مع علم بقية علماء العصر، فلا تعرف من أحدهم مخالفة ولا تأييد.
والأول القولي هو الحجة المسلمة، أما الثاني السكوتي فمختلف جداً. في اعتباره وفي درجة هذا الاعتبار وشرائطه.
3/5 - And ijma' is of two types: qawli (verbal) and sukuti (tacit). The qawli is by circulating opinions and explicit agreement from the scholars. The sukuti is that one of them gives a ruling while the rest of the scholars of the era know of it, and no opposition nor support is known from any of them. The first, the qawli, is the undisputed proof. As for the second, the sukuti, it is very much disputed regarding its validity, the degree of this validity, and its conditions.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage classifies ijma' into two types. Qawli ijma' occurs when scholars explicitly agree after discussing the issue; its authority is universally accepted. Sukuti ijma' occurs when a scholar issues a ruling and other scholars remain silent despite knowing about it, without explicit approval or disapproval. The author notes that the validity of sukuti ijma' is highly debated among scholars, including its conditions and the strength of its binding force. The text does not specify which positions are stronger, but the Hanafi school generally accepts sukuti ijma' as hujjah under certain conditions, such as widespread knowledge of the ruling and the ability to object without fear.

Key Terms
الإجماع القولي (al-ijmāʿ al-qawlī): الاتفاق الصريح من العلماء بعد تداول الرأي
الإجماع السكوتي (al-ijmāʿ al-sukūtī): أن يفتي أحدهم بحكم مع علم بقية علماء العصر، فلا تظهر مخالفة ولا تأييد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of sukuti ijma' compared to qawli ijma'?
A) Both are equally binding.
B) Sukuti ijma' is more reliable.
C) Qawli ijma' is undisputed while sukuti is highly disputed.
D) Qawli ijma' is not considered hujjah.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is that qawli ijma' relies on explicit agreement, whereas sukuti ijma' is inferred from silence and is subject to significant scholarly debate.

Historical Limitation of Ijma'
Explains why Ijma' became difficult after the first century

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ijma' is historically limited to the first Islamic century and evaluate its applicability in contemporary fatwa.

Core Idea
Ijma' required all mujtahids to gather; after Companions dispersed, universal consensus became impossible.

This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm explains a key historical reality: Ijma' (consensus) was feasible only when the Companions were concentrated in Medina under 'Umar's caliphate. Their later dispersion made general consultation impossible, so later claims of Ijma' are unreliable. This lesson explores how this historical limitation affects Hanafi fatwa methodology today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical condition
Read the passage and note what made Ijma' easy in the first era: the Companions were kept in Medina, enabling consultation.
Key: 'Umar prevented them from leaving.
2
Pinpoint the cause of limitation
Identify the event that ended this condition: the dispersal of Companions at the end of 'Uthman's caliphate to various provinces.
3
Infer the practical consequence
Understand that after dispersion, achieving Ijma' of all mujtahids became impossible, so later consensus claims are invalid.
This is a core principle in Hanafi usul: Ijma' is confined to the early period.
4
Apply to fatwa practice
Consider how a mufti handles new issues today: he cannot claim Ijma', so he relies on tarjih (preponderance) among existing views.
This lesson is foundational for understanding fatwa hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۳) المصادر الأساسية للفقه
وقد كان الإجماع في العصر الأول سهل الحصول لأن عمر رضي الله عنه في خلافته منع الصحابة أن يخرجوا من المدينة لتمكنه مشاورتهم فيما يحدث من أمور العلم أو السياسة، ولكنهم تفرَّقوا بعد ذلك أواخر خلافة عثمان في الأمصار، ونشأ على أيديهم علماء وفقهاء في أماكن متنائية في الحجاز واليمن ومصر والعراق والشام وغيرها؛ فلم يمكن بعد ذلك تحقق إجماع من المجتهدين لانقطاع إمكان الشورى العلمية العامة ولأن اتفاق علماء بلد واحد على حكم لا يعتبر إجماعاً.
Chapter (3): The Basic Sources of Fiqh. And Ijma' in the first era was easy to obtain because 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, during his caliphate prevented the Companions from leaving Medina to enable him to consult them regarding emerging matters of knowledge or politics, but they later dispersed at the end of 'Uthman's caliphate to the provinces, and scholars and jurists arose at their hands in distant places in Hijaz, Yemen, Egypt, Iraq, Syria, and others; so after that it was not possible to achieve Ijma' of the mujtahids because the possibility of general scholarly consultation was cut off, and because the agreement of the scholars of one country on a ruling is not considered Ijma'.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm discusses the historical limitation of Ijma' (consensus) as a source of law. It explains that during the first Islamic century, Ijma' was easily achievable because the Caliph 'Umar kept the Companions concentrated in Medina, facilitating consultation. However, after the Companions dispersed to various regions in the late Caliphate of 'Uthman, it became impossible to gather all mujtahids for a general consensus. Consequently, Ijma' is confined to the early period, and later scholars cannot rely on it for new issues. The passage underscores that Ijma' is not a living source for contemporary fatwa due to practical constraints.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): Consensus of all mujtahids of the age on a legal ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Zarqa consider Ijma' impractical after the first centuries of Islam?
A) Because mujtahids are no longer present
B) Because scholars dispersed and universal consultation became impossible
C) Because the Caliphs forbade it
D) Because Ijma' is not a valid source

Key Takeaway
Ijma' was historically possible only when mujtahids were centralized; after their dispersal, it became practically impossible, so later fatwa cannot rely on Ijma'.

Qiyas: The Fourth Source – Definition, Ranking, and Necessity
Defines Qiyas and establishes its role as the most productive fiqh source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas, explain why it ranks fourth after Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma', and justify its necessity using the finite-texts-infinite-events argument.

Core Idea
Texts are finite, events are infinite, so Qiyas is indispensable for Islamic legal methodology.

In this passage, al-Zarqa introduces qiyas (analogical reasoning) as the fourth primary source of fiqh. He explains its definition, its ranking relative to other sources, and why it is the most productive source for deriving rulings for new incidents. The discussion is grounded in both logical necessity (finite texts vs. infinite events) and early Islamic practice (the letter of Caliph Umar).

Guided Path
1
Define Qiyas Linguistically and Technically
Identify the key elements of the definition: ilhaq (attaching), asl and far' (original and new case), hukm (ruling), and 'illa (common cause). Note that the 'illa is the ratio legis that justifies the analogy.
The Arabic definition is: إلحاق أمر بآخر في الحكم الشرعي لاتحاد بينهما في العلة.
2
Locate Qiyas in the Source Hierarchy
Observe that qiyas is placed fourth after Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma'. Understand that it is still a primary source (masdar) but relies on the earlier sources for its validity. Note the comparison with Ijma': Ijma' is limited in scope, while qiyas is unlimited because it can be applied by each mujtahid individually.
Al-Zarqa says Ijma' is difficult to realize after the first era, so qiyas becomes more instrumental.
3
Grasp the Finiteness Argument
Analyze the reasoning: the Qur'an and Sunnah are finite (limited number of verses and hadith), but the events and transactions that occur in daily life are infinite. Since the finite cannot encompass the infinite, ijtihad via qiyas is necessary to derive rulings for every new case.
Al-Shahristani's quote reinforces the logical necessity of qiyas.
4
Examine the Evidence from Umar's Letter
Read the excerpt from Umar's letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Identify the instructions: 'Understanding, understanding... then know the similarities and counterparts, and measure matters by their likenesses.' This shows that qiyas was a recognized method in early Islamic judicial practice.
This letter is considered a foundational document for Islamic legal theory.
5
Appreciate the Productivity of Qiyas
Al-Zarqa states that qiyas is the most prolific (aghrar) source of fiqh rulings because it can generate rulings for countless new cases, unlike Ijma' which is circumscribed. This establishes qiyas as a dynamic tool for the evolution of fiqh.
The Hanafi school relies heavily on qiyas, making it a defining feature of Hanafi methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الرابع: القياس
٦/٣ - القياس هو : إلحاق أمر بآخر في الحكم الشرعي لاتحاد بينهما في العلة.
والقياس يأتي في المرتبة الرابعة بعد الكتاب والسنة والإجماع من حيث حُجيَّتُهُ في إثبات الأحكام الفقهية ولكنه أعظم أثراً من الإجماع في كثرة ما يرجع إليه من أحكام الفقه، لأن مسائل الإجماع محصورة ولم يتأت فيها زيادة لانصراف علماء المسلمين في مختلف الأقطار عن مبدأ الشورى العلمية العامة، ولتعذر تحققه بمعناه الكامل فيما بعد العصر الأول كما أوضحناه. أما القياس فلا يشترط فيه اتفاق كلمة العلماء، بل كل مجتهد يقيس بنظره الخاص في كل حادثة لا نصَّ عليها في الكتاب أو السنة ولا إجماع عليها .
ولا يخفى أن نصوص الكتاب والسنة محدودة متناهية والحوادث الواقعة والمتوقعة غير متناهية. فلا سبيل إلى إعطاء الحوادث والمعاملات الجديدة منازلها وأحكامها في فقه الشريعة إلا عن طريق الاجتهاد بالرأي الذي رأسه القياس فالقياس أغزر المصادر الفقهية في إثبات الأحكام الفرعية للحوادث : (۱)
وقد جاء في كتاب عمر بن الخطاب إلى أبي موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنهما يرشده إلى أصول القضاء وطريقته المثلى :
«الفهم الفهم فيما تلجلج في صدرك مما ليس في كتاب الله، ولا سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم اعرف الأشباه والأمثال، فَقس الأمور عند ذلك بنظائرها .. واعمد إلى أقربها إلى الله، وأشبهها بالحق». (۲)
(۱) يقول الشهرستاني في كتابه الملل والنحل: إن الحوادث والوقائع في العبادات والتصرفات مما لا يقبل الحصر والعد. ونعلم قطعاً أنه لم يرد في كل حادثة نص، ولا يتصور ذلك أيضاً. والنصوص إذا كانت متناهية، والوقائع غير متناهية وما لا يتناهى لا يضبطه ما يتناهى، علم قطعاً أن الاجتهاد والقياس واجب الاعتبار حتى يكون بصدد كل حادثة اجتهاد اهـ . الملل والنحل للشهرستاني، أول بحث الاختلاف في الأحكام الشرعية الاجتهادية). (۲) هذا الكتاب أرسله عمر إلى أبي موسى بعد ما ولاه. وهو يعد في نظر العلماء دستوراً عظيماً في سياسة القضاء وفقهه. وقد رأينا أن نثبته هنا بنصه، لأننا قد نحتاج إلى الاستشهاد به في مناسبات أخرى، وهو بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم من عبد الله عمر بن الخطاب أمير المؤمنين إلى عبد الله بن قيس: سلام عليك. أما بعد فإنّ القضاء فريضةٌ مُحْكمة، وسُنَّةٌ مُتَّبَعَة . فافهم إذا أدلى إليك الخصم بحجته، وأنفذ الحق إذا وضح لك، فإنه لا ينفع تكلم بحق لانفاذ له . آس بين الناس في مجلسك ووجهك وعدلك حتى لا يطمعَ شريف في حَيْفِك، ولا ييأس ضعيف من عدلك . البينة على من ادعى، واليمين على مَنْ أنكر . والصلح جائز بين المسلمين إلا صلحاً أحل حراماً أو حرم حلالاً. ولا يمنعنك قضاء قضيته بالأمس فراجعت فيه نفسك، وهديت فيه لرشدك : أن ترجع إلى الحق، فإن الحقَّ قديم، ولا يبطله شيء، ومراجعة الحقِّ خير من التمادي في الباطل . الفهم الفهم فيما تَلَجْلَجَ في صَدْرِكَ مما ليس في كتاب الله، ولا سنة النبي . ثم اعرف الأشباه والأمثال فقس الأمور عند ذلك بنظائرها، واعمد إلى أحبها
Fourth Topic: Qiyas (Analogical Reasoning). 6/3 - Qiyas is: Attaching one matter to another in legal ruling due to unity between them in the underlying cause. And Qiyas comes in the fourth rank after the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma' in terms of its authority in establishing fiqh rulings, but it has a greater impact than Ijma' in the abundance of rulings that refer to it, because issues of Ijma' are limited and no increase is possible due to the divergence of Muslim scholars in various regions from the principle of general scholarly consultation, and due to the difficulty of its realization in its complete sense after the first era, as we explained. As for Qiyas, the agreement of all scholars is not required; rather, each mujtahid measures by his own opinion in every new incident for which there is no text in the Book or Sunnah and no Ijma'. And it is not hidden that the texts of the Book and Sunnah are limited and finite, while actual and expected incidents are infinite. So there is no way to give new incidents and transactions their ranks and rulings in the fiqh of Shariah except through ijtihad by opinion, whose head is Qiyas. Thus Qiyas is the most prolific of fiqh sources in establishing subsidiary rulings for incidents. (1) And there came in the letter of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with them both, guiding him to the principles of judgment and its ideal method: 'Understanding, understanding regarding what troubles your heart for which there is nothing in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet, then know the similarities and counterparts, and measure matters by their likenesses... and aim for the one closest to Allah and most resembling the truth.' (2) (1) Al-Shahristani says in his book al-Milal wa al-Nihal: Incidents and occurrences in acts of worship and transactions are beyond enumeration. We know for certain that no text has come for every incident, and that is inconceivable. Since texts are finite, and occurrences are infinite, and what is infinite cannot be encompassed by what is finite, it is known with certainty that ijtihad and qiyas must be considered so that there is ijtihad for every incident. (Al-Milal wa al-Nihal by al-Shahristani, beginning of the discussion on disagreement in ijtihadi legal rulings.) (2) This letter was sent by 'Umar to Abu Musa after appointing him. It is considered by scholars as a great constitution in judicial policy and jurisprudence. We have seen fit to record it here in full, as we may need to cite it on other occasions. It is: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. From the servant of Allah, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, Commander of the Faithful, to 'Abdullah ibn Qays: Peace be upon you. To proceed: Indeed, judgment is a decisive obligation and a followed sunnah. Understand when the litigant presents his evidence to you, and enforce the truth when it becomes clear to you, for it is of no use to speak the truth without enforcement. Treat people equally in your assembly, your countenance, and your justice so that no noble person hopes for your bias and no weak person despairs of your justice. The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies. Reconciliation is permissible among Muslims except a reconciliation that makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful. And let no decision you made yesterday with which you later reconsidered and were guided to the right prevent you from returning to the truth, for truth is eternal and nothing nullifies it, and returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood. Understanding, understanding regarding what troubles your heart for which there is nothing in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet. Then know the similarities and counterparts, and measure matters by their likenesses, and aim for the one most beloved...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm defines Qiyas (analogical reasoning) as the fourth primary source of fiqh after the Qur'an, Sunnah, and Ijma'. The author emphasizes that while Ijma' is limited in scope, Qiyas is unlimited and necessary because the primary texts (nusus) are finite but occurrences are infinite. Therefore, every mujtahid may use Qiyas to derive rulings for new cases. The passage also cites the famous letter of Caliph 'Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari as evidence for the legitimacy of Qiyas in judicial practice. This letter is considered a foundational document in Islamic legal methodology. Al-Zarqa also quotes al-Shahristani to underscore the logical necessity of Qiyas. The lesson highlights that Qiyas is the most productive source of fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning: attaching one matter to another in legal ruling due to a common cause
العلة (al-ʿilla): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies the analogy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarqa, why is Qiyas considered a necessary source for fiqh?
A) Because the Qur'an and Sunnah are insufficient
B) Because texts are finite while events are infinite
C) Because Ijma' is impossible
D) Because all scholars agree on it

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is the indispensable fourth source of fiqh, enabling mujtahids to derive rulings for unlimited new events based on a shared cause with established cases.

Rational Necessity of Qiyas
Rational proof for necessity of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Shahristani's argument for the necessity of qiyas and explain why textual sources alone cannot cover all legal events.

Core Idea
Texts are finite, events are infinite—qiyas is indispensable for comprehensive Shariah.

This lesson explores the rational foundation for qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a source of Islamic law. The passage from al-Zarqa's Madkhal presents a logical proof by al-Shahristani that because the number of legal events is infinite and the revealed texts are finite, qiyas and ijtihad are necessary to derive rulings for new cases. This establishes qiyas as an essential tool in the Hanafi juristic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the finite/infinite problem
Understand that revealed texts (Quran and Sunnah) are limited in number, while legal events and new cases are unlimited. This sets up the need for a method to extend rulings.
Al-Shahristani states this explicitly: 'al-nusus idha kanat mutanahiyah, wa al-waqa'i ghayru mutanahiyah'.
2
Grasp the necessity of qiyas
Since the finite cannot encompass the infinite, a rational method of analogy (qiyas) must be employed to ensure every event has a legal ruling. Without it, many cases would remain unregulated.
Author says: 'al-ijtihad wa al-qiyas wajib al-i'tibar'.
3
Relate to Hanafi methodology
The Hanafi madhhab relies heavily on qiyas and ra'y, and this rational proof justifies such reliance. Qiyas becomes a primary source for deriving subsidiary rulings.
This aligns with the school's identity as 'ahl al-ra'y'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
الجديدة منازلها وأحكامها في فقه الشريعة إلا عن طريق الاجتهاد بالرأي (1) الذي رأسه القياس فالقياس أغزر المصادر الفقهية في إثبات الأحكام الفرعية للحوادث :
رضي
وقد جاء في كتاب عمر بن الخطاب إلى أبي موسى الله عنهما يرشده إلى أصول القضاء وطريقته المثلى :
الأشعري
«الفهم الفهم فيما تلجلج في صدرك مما ليس في كتاب الله، ولا سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم اعرف الأشباه والأمثال، فَقس الأمور عند ذلك بنظائرها .. واعمد إلى أقربها إلى الله، وأشبهها بالحق»(۲).
* (۱) يقول الشهرستاني في كتابه الملل والنحل: إن الحوادث والوقائع في العبادات والتصرفات مما لا يقبل الحصر والعد. ونعلم قطعاً أنه لم يرد في كل حادثة نص، ولا يتصور ذلك أيضاً. والنصوص إذا كانت متناهية، والوقائع غير متناهية وما لا يتناهى لا يضبطه ما يتناهى، علم قطعاً أن الاجتهاد والقياس واجب الاعتبار حتى يكون بصدد كل حادثة اجتهاد اهـ . الملل والنحل للشهرستاني، أول بحث الاختلاف في الأحكام الشرعية الاجتهادية).
(۲) هذا الكتاب أرسله عمر إلى أبي موسى بعد ما ولاه. وهو يعد في نظر العلماء دستوراً عظيماً في سياسة القضاء وفقهه. وقد رأينا أن نثبته هنا بنصه، لأننا قد نحتاج إلى الاستشهاد به في مناسبات أخرى، وهو بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم من عبد الله عمر بن الخطاب أمير المؤمنين إلى عبد الله بن قيس: سلام عليك. أما بعد فإنّ القضاء فريضةٌ مُحْكمة، وسُنَّةٌ متَّبَعَة . فافهم إذا أدلى إليك الخصم بحجته، وأنفذ الحق إذا وضح لك، فإنه لا ينفع تكلم بحق لانفاذ له .
.
آس بين الناس في مجلسك ووجهك وعدلك حتى لا يطمعَ شريف في حَيْفِك، ولا ييأس ضعيف من عدلك .
البينة على من ادعى، واليمين على مَنْ أنكر .
والصلح جائز بين المسلمين إلا صلحاً أحل حراماً أو حرم حلالاً. ولا يمنعنك قضاء قضيته بالأمس فراجعت فيه نفسك، وهديت فيه لرشدك : أن ترجع إلى الحق، فإن الحقِّ ،قديم، ولا يبطله شيء، ومراجعة الحقِّ خير من التمادي في الباطل . الفهم الفهم فيما تَلَجْلَجَ في صَدْرِكَ مما ليس في كتاب الله ، ولا سنة النبي . ثم اعرف الأشباه والأمثال فقس الأمور عند ذلك بنظائرها، واعمد إلى أحبها إلى الله، وأشبهها بالحق فيما ترى فاتبعه. واجعَلْ لمن ادعى حقاً غائباً أو بينةً أمداً ينتهي إليه ، فإِن أَحضَرَ بَيْنَتَهُ أَخَذْتَ له بحقه، وإلا وجهت عليه القضاء، فإن ذلك أنفى للشك، وأجلى للعمى، وأبلغ في العُذر. المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض إلا مجلوداً في حد، أو مُجَرَّباً عليه شهادة زور ، أو ظنيناً في ولاء أو نسب . فإنّ الله قد تولى منكم السرائر، ودرأ عنكم بالبينات والأيمان . وإياك والقلق والضَّجَرَ والتأذُيَ بالخصوم والتنكَّرَ للخصوم في مواطن الحق التي يوجب الله بها الأجر، ويحسِنُ بها الذكر. فإنه من يصلح ،نِيْتَه فيما بينه وبين الله يكفه الله ما بينه وبين الناس. ومن تزين للناس بما يعلمُ الله منه غير ذلك يَشِنهُ الله فما ظنك بثواب عند الله عز وجل في عاجل رزقه وخزائن ،رحمته والسلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته . (ر) جمهرة رسائل العرب للأستاذ أحمد زكي صفوة ج ١ ص / ٢٥٢/ رقم الرسالة / ٢١٤/ . وإعلام الموقعين لابن القيم ج /٩٩/، والكامل للمبرد ج ١ /٩/ والبيان والتبيين بشرح السندوبي الطبعة الثانية ج ۲ ص / ٣٧). وقد تولى ابن القيم شرحه بإسهاب في مواطن عديدة من إعلام الموقعين (ج) اص١٠٠ و ج ۲ ص / ٢٨٤ - ٢٩٠.

The Second Chapter: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. The new [events] their ranks and rulings in the fiqh of Shariah can only be through ijtihad by opinion (1) whose head is qiyas. Qiyas is the most abundant of juristic sources in establishing subsidiary rulings for incidents. And it has come in the letter of Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with them both, guiding him to the principles of judiciary and its ideal method: 'Understanding, understanding concerning what perplexes your breast of what is not in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, then know the similarities and analogues, then measure matters accordingly by their parallels... and aim for the closest to Allah and the most resembling of the truth.' (2) * (1) Al-Shahristani says in his book Al-Milal wa al-Nihal: Indeed, events and incidents in acts of worship and transactions are not susceptible to enumeration. And we know definitively that there has not come a text for every event, nor is that conceivable. And texts are finite, while events are infinite, and what is infinite cannot be encompassed by what is finite. One knows definitively that ijtihad and qiyas are necessarily regarded so that for every event there is an ijtihad. End quote. Al-Milal wa al-Nihal, first discussion of difference in ijtihadi legal rulings. (2) This letter was sent by Umar to Abu Musa after he appointed him. It is considered by scholars as a great constitution in the policy of judiciary and its fiqh. We have seen fit to record it here in its text because we may need to cite it on other occasions. It is: 'In the name of Allah, the Merciful, the Compassionate. From the servant of Allah, Umar ibn al-Khattab, Commander of the Faithful, to Abdullah ibn Qais: Peace be upon you. To proceed: Verily judgment is an established obligation and a followed Sunnah. So understand when the litigant presents his argument to you, and execute the truth when it becomes clear to you, for indeed speaking the truth without execution does not benefit. Be equal with people in your assembly, your face, and your justice, so that no noble person hopes for partiality from you, and no weak person despairs of your justice. The burden of proof is upon the claimant, and the oath is upon the denier. And reconciliation is permissible among Muslims except a reconciliation that permits the forbidden or forbids the lawful. And let not a judgment you passed yesterday prevent you from returning to the truth if you reconsider yourself and are guided to your right path, for the truth is ancient and nothing invalidates it, and returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood. Understanding, understanding concerning what perplexes your breast of what is not in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet. Then know the similarities and analogues, then measure matters accordingly by their parallels, and aim for the most beloved to Allah and the most resembling of the truth in what you see, and follow it. And set for one who claims a right that is absent or evidence a term that ends at it. If he brings his evidence, take his right for him; otherwise, pass the judgment against him. Indeed, that is more effective in dispelling doubt, more revealing of blindness, and more effective in excusing. Muslims are reliable one over another, except one who has been flogged for a hadd punishment, or one who has been experienced bearing false witness, or one who is suspected regarding patronage or lineage. For Allah has taken charge of your secrets from you and warded off from you through evidence and oaths. Beware of anxiety, irritation, and annoyance with litigants, and mistreatment of them in the places of truth through which Allah grants reward and beautifies remembrance. For one who rectifies his intention between himself and Allah, Allah will suffice him between himself and people. And one who beautifies himself for people while Allah knows from him other than that, Allah will disgrace him. So what do you think of reward with Allah Almighty in the immediate provision of His sustenance and the treasures of His mercy? And peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' (Sources) And it has been expanded in its extraction from the books of the purified Sunnah, fiqh, literature, history, and biographies by the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah in the journal of the College of Usul al-Din, issue 4, year 1402, under the title 'Verification of the Establishment of the Letter of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari concerning the Judiciary, and in It the Use of Qiyas.' Explanation of some terms in the letter: 'If he presents to you' from al-idla' with the proof, i.e., the establishment of evidence. 'And execute' from al-inafadh, i.e., direct the judgment and make it effective, i.e., follow up the judgment with execution until the right-holder receives his right. 'Be equal' (as) is a command for equality, i.e., make some an example of others without distinction. 'Perplexes' (taljalaj): wavers and is difficult. 'Warded off' (dara): repelled and prevented, and in the prophetic hadith: 'Avert the hudud punishments by doubts.' (1) See the book 'History of Islamic Legislation' by the professors al-Sabki, al-Sayis, and al-Barbari, p. 6.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm discusses the necessity and foundational role of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Islamic jurisprudence. The author opens by asserting that new events can only be legally governed through ijtihad bi al-ra'y (reasoned opinion), the pinnacle of which is qiyas. He then quotes al-Shahristani's rational proof: texts are finite, events are infinite, so a finite source cannot cover all infinite events; thus qiyas and ijtihad are indispensable. The heart of the passage is the famous letter of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which serves as an early methodological directive for judges. The letter instructs judges to first rely on Quran and Sunnah, but when these are silent, to use 'ashbah wa amthal' (similar cases) and qiyas (measurement by parallels). It also contains procedural principles like 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' (burden of proof on claimant, oath on denier) and encouragement to return to truth. The author then provides a commentary explaining key terms from the letter. The passage establishes qiyas as a legitimate and essential source of fiqh from the earliest generation, rooted in the practice of the Companions and the explicit instruction of Umar. For the Hanafi madhhab, this is a cornerstone: the school relies heavily on qiyas and ra'y, and the letter of Umar is often cited as a precedent for such methodology.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illah).
الاجتهاد بالرأي (al-ijtihad bi al-ra'y): Reasoned independent legal reasoning, often associated with qiyas and istihsan.
الأشباه والأمثال (al-ashbah wa al-amthal): Similar cases and analogues used as the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Shahristani, why is qiyas necessary in Islamic jurisprudence?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands it.
B) Because texts are finite and events are infinite.
C) Because the Companions unanimously agreed on it.
D) Because it is the only way to ensure consistency in rulings.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is not optional but an essential tool for Islamic law because revealed texts cannot cover all future events.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
beginner
8 min
The Letter of Umar: A Fatwa Methodology
Methodological instructions for judges and muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key methodological instructions in Umar's letter and explain how they establish qiyas as a legitimate source for iftaa.

Core Idea
Umar's letter instructs judges to use 'ashbah wa amthal' and qiyas when texts are silent — a foundational methodology for iftaa.

This lesson examines the famous letter of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab to his judge Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The letter provides a comprehensive guide to judicial reasoning, emphasizing the use of analogy (qiyas) when the Quran and Sunnah do not provide explicit rulings. It also includes foundational procedural principles such as the burden of proof and the importance of returning to truth. For the Hanafi madhhab, this letter is a key evidence for the legitimacy of qiyas and ra'y.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the letter
Understand that Umar wrote this letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, who was appointed as a judge. The letter is a guide to proper legal reasoning and procedure.
Al-Zarqa calls it a 'great constitution in the policy of judiciary'.
2
Extract the instruction on qiyas
Focus on the sentence: 'then know the similarities and analogues, then measure matters accordingly by their parallels.' This is a direct command to use analogical reasoning when no explicit text exists.
This is the earliest known endorsement of qiyas by a Caliph in Islamic history.
3
Note other key procedural principles
The letter also establishes rules: burden of proof on the claimant, oath on the denier, permissible reconciliation, revisiting judgments for truth, equality of litigants, and caution in accepting witnesses.
These principles are still used in Islamic courts and fatwa institutions.
4
Relate to Hanafi iftaa methodology
The Hanafi school uses this letter as a primary evidence that qiyas is a legitimate source. It demonstrates that the early Community, under the guidance of Umar, practiced ijtihad with ra'y and qiyas.
Hanafi fuqaha often cite this letter in discussions on the validity of qiyas.

الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي

The Second Chapter: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. The new [events] their ranks and rulings in the fiqh of Shariah can only be through ijtihad by opinion (1) whose head is qiyas. Qiyas is the most abundant of juristic sources in establishing subsidiary rulings for incidents. And it has come in the letter of Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with them both, guiding him to the principles of judiciary and its ideal method: 'Understanding, understanding concerning what perplexes your breast of what is not in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, then know the similarities and analogues, then measure matters accordingly by their parallels... and aim for the closest to Allah and the most resembling of the truth.' (2) * (1) Al-Shahristani says in his book Al-Milal wa al-Nihal: Indeed, events and incidents in acts of worship and transactions are not susceptible to enumeration. And we know definitively that there has not come a text for every event, nor is that conceivable. And texts are finite, while events are infinite, and what is infinite cannot be encompassed by what is finite. One knows definitively that ijtihad and qiyas are necessarily regarded so that for every event there is an ijtihad. End quote. Al-Milal wa al-Nihal, first discussion of difference in ijtihadi legal rulings. (2) This letter was sent by Umar to Abu Musa after he appointed him. It is considered by scholars as a great constitution in the policy of judiciary and its fiqh. We have seen fit to record it here in its text because we may need to cite it on other occasions. It is: 'In the name of Allah, the Merciful, the Compassionate. From the servant of Allah, Umar ibn al-Khattab, Commander of the Faithful, to Abdullah ibn Qais: Peace be upon you. To proceed: Verily judgment is an established obligation and a followed Sunnah. So understand when the litigant presents his argument to you, and execute the truth when it becomes clear to you, for indeed speaking the truth without execution does not benefit. Be equal with people in your assembly, your face, and your justice, so that no noble person hopes for partiality from you, and no weak person despairs of your justice. The burden of proof is upon the claimant, and the oath is upon the denier. And reconciliation is permissible among Muslims except a reconciliation that permits the forbidden or forbids the lawful. And let not a judgment you passed yesterday prevent you from returning to the truth if you reconsider yourself and are guided to your right path, for the truth is ancient and nothing invalidates it, and returning to the truth is better than persisting in falsehood. Understanding, understanding concerning what perplexes your breast of what is not in the Book of Allah nor the Sunnah of the Prophet. Then know the similarities and analogues, then measure matters accordingly by their parallels, and aim for the most beloved to Allah and the most resembling of the truth in what you see, and follow it. And set for one who claims a right that is absent or evidence a term that ends at it. If he brings his evidence, take his right for him; otherwise, pass the judgment against him. Indeed, that is more effective in dispelling doubt, more revealing of blindness, and more effective in excusing. Muslims are reliable one over another, except one who has been flogged for a hadd punishment, or one who has been experienced bearing false witness, or one who is suspected regarding patronage or lineage. For Allah has taken charge of your secrets from you and warded off from you through evidence and oaths. Beware of anxiety, irritation, and annoyance with litigants, and mistreatment of them in the places of truth through which Allah grants reward and beautifies remembrance. For one who rectifies his intention between himself and Allah, Allah will suffice him between himself and people. And one who beautifies himself for people while Allah knows from him other than that, Allah will disgrace him. So what do you think of reward with Allah Almighty in the immediate provision of His sustenance and the treasures of His mercy? And peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' (Sources) And it has been expanded in its extraction from the books of the purified Sunnah, fiqh, literature, history, and biographies by the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah in the journal of the College of Usul al-Din, issue 4, year 1402, under the title 'Verification of the Establishment of the Letter of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari concerning the Judiciary, and in It the Use of Qiyas.' Explanation of some terms in the letter: 'If he presents to you' from al-idla' with the proof, i.e., the establishment of evidence. 'And execute' from al-inafadh, i.e., direct the judgment and make it effective, i.e., follow up the judgment with execution until the right-holder receives his right. 'Be equal' (as) is a command for equality, i.e., make some an example of others without distinction. 'Perplexes' (taljalaj): wavers and is difficult. 'Warded off' (dara): repelled and prevented, and in the prophetic hadith: 'Avert the hudud punishments by doubts.' (1) See the book 'History of Islamic Legislation' by the professors al-Sabki, al-Sayis, and al-Barbari, p. 6.

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm discusses the necessity and foundational role of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Islamic jurisprudence. The author opens by asserting that new events can only be legally governed through ijtihad bi al-ra'y (reasoned opinion), the pinnacle of which is qiyas. He then quotes al-Shahristani's rational proof: texts are finite, events are infinite, so a finite source cannot cover all infinite events; thus qiyas and ijtihad are indispensable. The heart of the passage is the famous letter of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which serves as an early methodological directive for judges. The letter instructs judges to first rely on Quran and Sunnah, but when these are silent, to use 'ashbah wa amthal' (similar cases) and qiyas (measurement by parallels). It also contains procedural principles like 'al-bayyinah 'ala man idda'a wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' (burden of proof on claimant, oath on denier) and encouragement to return to truth. The author then provides a commentary explaining key terms from the letter. The passage establishes qiyas as a legitimate and essential source of fiqh from the earliest generation, rooted in the practice of the Companions and the explicit instruction of Umar. For the Hanafi madhhab, this is a cornerstone: the school relies heavily on qiyas and ra'y, and the letter of Umar is often cited as a precedent for such methodology.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illah).
الاجتهاد بالرأي (al-ijtihad bi al-ra'y): Reasoned independent legal reasoning, often associated with qiyas and istihsan.
الأشباه والأمثال (al-ashbah wa al-amthal): Similar cases and analogues used as the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Umar's letter, what should a judge do when a case is not explicitly covered by the Quran or Sunnah?
A) Refuse to judge and wait for a new revelation.
B) Consult other judges and issue a consensus opinion.
C) Identify similar cases and use analogical reasoning (qiyas).
D) Apply the principle of istihsan based on public interest.

Key Takeaway
Umar's letter provides an early and authoritative endorsement of qiyas as a legitimate source of law, forming a key part of the Hanafi methodological foundation.

The Stated Causes (ʿIllal) in Quran and Sunnah: Foundation for Qiyas
Explaining how Quran and Sunnah state causes to enable qiyas, citing Umar's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Quran and Sunnah state causes for rulings and explain how this enables qiyas, using the letter of ʿUmar as a precedent.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah state causes to allow qiyas on similar cases across time.

This passage reveals a key feature of Islamic legal texts: they often state the causes (ʿillal) behind rulings. This is not accidental; it opens the door for analogical reasoning (qiyas). The author then invokes the famous letter of Caliph ʿUmar to his judge Abu Mūsā al-Ashʿarī, which explicitly instructs the use of qiyas. This lesson unpacks how the Hanafi school relies on this methodology to derive rulings for new situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic and Prophetic style
Recognize that Quran and Sunnah often state the causes ('illal) and general Sharia objectives behind rulings.
This is not always explicit, but the text itself indicates the presence of a cause.
2
Understand the purpose: enabling qiyas
The stated causes are meant to allow scholars to apply the same ruling to similar cases in any time, via analogical reasoning.
Without the 'illa, qiyas would be arbitrary.
3
Examine the letter of ʿUmar as a primary source
The letter commands 'alayka bil-qiyas' (adhere to analogy) and instructs the judge to compare cases to the truth.
This letter is a strong proof that qiyas was practiced by the Companions.
4
Connect to Hanafi usul methodology
In Hanafi thought, the 'illa must be explicit or derived through istinbat; this letter supports the use of qiyas as a legitimate source.
The Hanafi school uses such texts to argue for the validity and necessity of qiyas.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد كان من أسلوب النصوص المعهودة في الكتاب والسنة أن تنص غالباً على علل الأحكام الواردة فيها، والغايات الشرعية العامة المقصودة منها، ليمكن تطبيق أمثالها وأشباهها عليها في كل زمن. ونصوص الكتاب معظمها كليّ عام إجمالي كما رأينا، فانفتح بذلك طريق لقياس غير المنصوص على ما هو منصوص، وإعطائه حكمه عند اتحاد العلة أو السبب فيهما. فعليك بالقياس، وأشبهها بالحق فيما ترى فاتبعه. واجعَلْ لمن ادعى حقاً غائباً أو بينةً أمداً ينتهي إليه، فإِن أَحضَرَ بَيْنَتَهُ أَخَذْتَ له بحقه، وإلا وجهت عليه القضاء، فإن ذلك أنفى للشك، وأجلى للعمى، وأبلغ في العُذر. المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض إلا مجلوداً في حد، أو مُجَرَّباً عليه شهادة زور، أو ظنيناً في ولاء أو نسب. فإنّ الله قد تولى منكم السرائر، ودرأ عنكم بالبينات والأيمان. وإياك والقلق والضَّجَرَ والتأذُيَ بالخصوم والتنكَّرَ للخصوم في مواطن الحق التي يوجب الله بها الأجر، ويحسِنُ بها الذكر. فإنه من يصلح نِيْتَه فيما بينه وبين الله يكفه الله ما بينه وبين الناس. ومن تزين للناس بما يعلمُ الله منه غير ذلك يَشِنهُ الله فما ظنك بثواب عند الله عز وجل في عاجل رزقه وخزائن رحمته والسلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته.
And it was from the established style of the texts in the Book and the Sunnah that they often state the causes of the rulings contained therein, and the general Sharia objectives intended from them, so that their likes and similar cases can be applied to them in every time. And the texts of the Book are mostly general and comprehensive as we have seen, so thereby the path was opened for analogical reasoning of what is not stipulated to what is stipulated, and giving it its ruling when the cause or reason is unified in both. So adhere to analogy, and compare it to the truth as you see it and follow it. And set a term for whoever claims a right or evidence that is absent, and if he brings his evidence then take for him his right, otherwise render judgment against him, for that is more repelling of doubt, more clarifying of blindness, and more effective in excuse. Muslims are trustworthy to each other except one who has been flogged for a hadd punishment, or one who has been experienced in false testimony, or one who is suspected in loyalty or lineage. For Allah has taken charge of your inner secrets, and has averted from you through clear proofs and oaths. And beware of anxiety, annoyance, and taking offense at litigants, and of showing antagonism towards litigants in places of truth where Allah grants reward and gives good repute. For whoever sets right his intention in what is between him and Allah, Allah will suffice him in what is between him and people. And whoever adorns himself for people with what Allah knows otherwise of him, Allah will disgrace him. So what is your thought of the reward from Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, in the immediate sustenance and treasures of His mercy. And peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.

Commentary
This passage is a philosophical discussion of the methodology of Islamic law. It begins by noting that the Quran and Sunnah typically state the 'illa (cause) behind rulings and their general Sharia objectives. This is not accidental; it enables scholars to apply analogical reasoning (qiyas) to new situations. The author then cites the famous letter of Caliph Umar to his judge Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which is a cornerstone in Islamic judicial theory. In the letter, Umar instructs the judge to use analogy ('qiyas'), to compare cases to the truth, and to follow what is more similar to the truth. The letter also contains practical judicial instructions about evidence, deadlines, and the conduct of judges. The Hanafi school views this letter as a strong precedent for the use of qiyas, since it comes from a rightly guided caliph and a Companion of the Prophet. The passage overall establishes that qiyas is not a human innovation but a method endorsed by the early authorities.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The effective cause or ratio legis behind a legal ruling, which provides the basis for qiyas.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared 'illa.

Seven Examples of Qiyas: From Text to New Cases
Illustrating the application of qiyas through seven examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas methodology: given a textual ruling and a new case, identify the shared 'illa and derive the analogous ruling.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends divine law to new cases by pinpointing the underlying cause—an indispensable tool for the mufti.

Qiyas is a cornerstone of Hanafi istinbat, allowing the jurist to go beyond the literal text when the cause ('illa) is the same. In this lesson, we study seven classical examples from Islamic jurisprudence that demonstrate how fuqaha' analogized from one ruling to another. Pay close attention to how the 'illa is identified in each case—this skill is crucial for fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl) and its textual ruling
Locate the primary text (Quran or Sunnah) that provides a clear ruling. This is the starting point for analogy.
Example 1: Quran 62:9 prohibits sale during Friday prayer.
2
Identify the new case (far') without direct text
Find a contemporary or unaddressed situation that lacks an explicit ruling but resembles the original.
Example 1: Other contracts like ijarah (lease) during Friday prayer.
3
Extract the 'illa (effective cause) from the original case
Determine the reason behind the ruling—what characteristic or purpose justifies the hukm. The 'illa must be suitable for extension.
Example 1: Distraction from Friday prayer and sermon is the 'illa.
4
Verify the 'illa is present in the new case
Confirm that the new case shares the same cause. If the cause is absent, qiyas is invalid.
All commercial contracts share the same distracting effect.
5
Derive the ruling for the new case
Apply the original ruling to the new case based on the shared 'illa. The ruling is the same unless overridden by a stronger source like istihsan.
Result: All contracts are invalid (batil) during Friday prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
المنصوص على ما هو منصوص، وإعطائه حكمه عند اتحاد العلة أو السبب فيهما .

۷/۳ - أمثلة القياس :
إن وقائع القياس في فقه الشريعة الإسلامية لا يمكن حصرها، فإنَّ منها يتكون الجانب الأعظم من الفقه ولا يزال القياس يُعمل باستمرار في كل حادثة جديدة في نوعها لا نص عليها .
غير أننا نضرب للإيضاح الأمثلة التالية:

1 - ورد النص القرآني في سورة الجمعة ٩/٦٢ بالنهي عن البيع وقت الأذان للصلاة يوم الجمعة، فقاسَ الفقهاء عليه حرمة التعاقد بعقود أخرى كالإجارة مثلاً، لأنَّ علة النهي أنّ البيع يلهي المتبايعين عن المبادرة والتهيؤ لصلاة الجمعة التي تتقدمها خطبة عامة توجيهية ومواعظ من الإمام . . وهذا السبب موجود في جميع الأعمال التجارية وسائر العقود الأخرى غير : البيع، وإن كانت صفقات البيع هي الأكثر وقوعاً في الأسواق. وقد حكم . معظم الفقهاء ببطلان البيع وسواه من العقود وقت أذان الجمعة.

۲ - ورد في الشريعة الإسلامية نصوص وأحكام بشأن وصي اليتيم عينت وضعه الحقوقي ومسؤوليته وصلاحيته، فقاس الفقهاء على أحكام الوصي أحكام متولي الوقف للشبه المستحكم بين الوظيفتين، كما قاسوا كثيراً من أحكام الوقف نفسه على أحكام الوصية. فقرروا حجر الإنسان عن أن يَقِفَ في مرض موته أكثر من ثلث ماله إلا بإجازة الورثة، قياساً على هذا الحجر الذي ورد في الشريعة بشأن الوصية لأنَّ كليهما تبرع؛ حتى قال : الفقهاء: إنَّ معظم أحكام الوقف تُسْتَقَى من الوصية.

٣ - ورد في الشريعة نصوص كثيرة في أحكام البيع أكثر مما ورد بشأن الإجارة، فقاس الفقهاء كثيراً من أحكام الإجارة على أحكام البيع لأنها في معناه إذ هي في الحقيقة بيع المنافع .

٤ - ورد في الشريعة نصوص تجيز الوكالة الخاصة بشأن مخصوص وتثبت لها أحكاماً معينة معروفة . فقاس فقهاء الحنفية عليها الوكالة العامة في الجواز والأحكام ولم يروا بأساً بعدم تعيين الأعمال الموكل بها وجهالتها عند العقد في هذه الوكالة العامة، لأنَّ العموم يجعل المجهول كالمعلوم ويحسم النزاع بخلاف الوكالة الخاصة إذا جهل موضوعها، كمن قال الآخر : وكلتك في بعض أعمالي فإنها غير جائزة باتفاق الفقهاء.

٥ - وكذلك قاسوا أيضاً على عقد التوكيل إجازة الإنسان تصرفاً في بعض حقوقه صَدَر من آخر فضولاً عنه دون سابق توكيل منه، فقرروا أنَّ الإجازة اللاحقة تعتبر كالوكالة السابقة؛ فيصبح بهذه الإجازة تصرف الفضولي (۱) نافذاً على المجيز كعمل الوكيل بمقتضى وكالة سابقة .

٦ - ثبت في أحكام الشريعة أنَّ الأجير مُجْبَرٌ على القيام بما استُؤْجِرَ عليه فقاس الفقهاء عليه حكم الوكيل بالأجرة، فاعتبروه مُخبراً على القيام بما وكل به، لأنه بتقاضيه الأجر أصبح كالأجير، وإن كانت الوكالة في الأصل عقداً غير لازم أي لا يوجب إلزام الوكيل بالعمل .

٧ - ثبت بنصوص الشريعة أنَّ مَنْ غَصَبَ شيئاً وَجَب عليه رد عينه ما عنده، فإنْ تَلِفَ المغصوب يضمن الغاصب للمالك مثله أو قيمته، وينتقل حق المالك إلى هذا التضمين عوضاً عن الأصل الهالك؛ وذلك بقوله : على اليد ما أخذت حتى تؤديه»(۲).
فقاس فقهاء الحنفية على هلاك المغصوب ما لو أحدث فيه الغاصب له به اسم جدید، كما لو غَصَب قطعة فولاذ فصنعها سيفاً، تغييراً يحدث أو طحن الحنطة المغصوبة حتى صارت دقيقاً، فاعتبروا هذا التغيير
(1) لمعرفة معنى الفضولي انظر ما سيأتي (ف ٥/٣٨ سابعاً). (۲) ر ف ۲/۱۰ ب. والحديث رواه أحمد والنسائي وابن ماجه والحاكم من حديث الحسن عن سمرة. ورواه أبو داود والترمذي بلفظ : حتى تؤدي والحسن مختلف في سماعه من سمرة. (ر ): التلخيص الحبير ٥٣/٣).
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
[The definition of qiyas:] applying the ruling of a text to something not textually stipulated, giving it the same ruling when the cause (illa) or reason is unified between them.

7/3 - Examples of Qiyas:
Indeed, the instances of qiyas in the jurisprudence of Islamic law cannot be enumerated, for the greater part of fiqh consists of them, and qiyas continues to be applied constantly to every new incident of a type not covered by a text.
Nevertheless, we give the following examples for clarification:

1 - The Quranic text in Surah al-Jumu'ah (62:9) prohibits selling at the time of the call to prayer on Friday. The jurists analogically deduced from it the prohibition of contracting other contracts, such as ijarah (lease), because the cause of the prohibition is that selling distracts the buyers and sellers from hastening and preparing for the Friday prayer, which is preceded by a general instructive sermon and admonitions from the imam... This reason exists in all commercial activities and other contracts besides selling, even though sales transactions are the most common in markets. Most jurists ruled that selling and other contracts are invalid at the time of the Friday call to prayer.

2 - Islamic law contains texts and rulings concerning the guardian of an orphan, defining his legal status, responsibility, and capacity. The jurists analogically applied the rulings of the guardian to the rulings of the administrator of a waqf (endowment) due to the strong similarity between the two functions. Likewise, they analogically applied many rulings of waqf itself to the rulings of bequest (wasiyya). They thus ruled that a person is restricted from endowing more than one-third of his wealth during his death illness without the consent of the heirs, based on analogy with this restriction in the law regarding bequest, because both are donations. For this reason, the jurists said: Most rulings of waqf are derived from bequest.

3 - Islamic law contains many texts on the rulings of sale, more than those on ijarah. The jurists analogically applied many rulings of ijarah to the rulings of sale because ijarah is similar in meaning to sale, as it is in reality a sale of benefits.

4 - Islamic law contains texts that permit special agency (wikala khassa) for a specific matter and establish certain known rulings for it. The Hanafi jurists analogically applied these to general agency (wikala 'amma) in terms of permissibility and rulings. They saw no objection to not specifying the delegated tasks and their being unknown at the time of contract in this general agency, because generality makes the unknown like the known and resolves disputes, unlike special agency if its subject matter is unknown, such as when someone says to another: "I delegate you for some of my affairs" — this is not permissible by agreement of the jurists.

5 - Likewise, they also analogically applied to the contract of agency the ratification (ijaza) by a person of an action in some of his rights performed by a stranger (fuduli) without prior delegation from him. They ruled that subsequent ratification is considered like prior agency; thus, by this ratification, the action of the stranger becomes binding on the ratifier, like the action of an agent under a prior agency.

6 - It is established in the rulings of Islamic law that a hired worker (ajir) is compelled to perform the work for which he was hired. The jurists analogically applied this to the ruling of a paid agent (wakil bi ujra), considering him compelled to perform the task for which he was delegated, because by receiving a fee he becomes like a hired worker, even though agency is originally a non-binding contract that does not obligate the agent to work.

7 - It is established by the texts of Islamic law that whoever usurps (ghasb) something must return its substance ('ayn) if it is still in his possession; if the usurped item perishes, the usurper must guarantee (damān) its equivalent (mithl) or value (qima) to the owner, and the owner's right transfers to this compensation in place of the original that perished. This is based on the saying: "Liability rests on the hand that took until it returns it."
The Hanafi jurists analogically applied the case of the usurped item's perishing to a case where the usurper brings about a new name (i.e., transforms it), such as if he usurps a piece of steel and makes it into a sword, or grinds usurped wheat until it becomes flour. They considered this transformation as a legal change equivalent to perishing, entailing the same guarantee.
(1) For the meaning of fuduli, see what will come later (section 5/38, seventh). (2) See section 2/10 b. The hadith was narrated by Ahmad, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim from the hadith of al-Hasan from Samura. It was also narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi with the wording: "until you return it" and there is disagreement about al-Hasan's hearing from Samura. (See: al-Talkhis al-Habir 3/53).
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is the core of the author's exposition on qiyas as a source of Islamic law. After defining qiyas as extending a ruling from a textual case to a new case sharing the same 'illa (cause), he provides seven concrete examples showing how fuqaha' (especially Hanafis) apply qiyas. 

Example 1: The Quranic prohibition of sales during Friday prayer is extended to all contracts (like ijarah) because the 'illa—distraction from prayer—is common. Most jurists rule that such contracts are invalid (batil) at that time.

Example 2: The rules for an orphan's guardian (wasi) are extended to the administrator of a waqf (mutawalli) due to functional similarity. Similarly, waqf rulings are analogized to bequests (wasiyya), so endowing more than one-third in death illness requires heirs' consent.

Example 3: Since ijarah is sale of benefits, its rulings are largely analogized from the more detailed sale rules.

Example 4 (Hanafi-specific): Special agency (wikala khassa) requires specifying the task; the Hanafis extend its permissibility to general agency (wikala 'amma) where tasks are unspecified, because generality removes uncertainty—unlike special agency where ambiguity invalidates the contract.

Example 5: Subsequent ratification (ijaza) of a fuduli's (unauthorized agent) act is analogized to prior agency, making the act binding on the ratifier.

Example 6: A hired worker must perform; analogically, a paid agent (wakil bi ujra) is compelled to work, even though ordinary agency is non-binding.

Example 7: If a usurper (ghasib) transforms the item (e.g., steel into sword, wheat into flour), the Hanafis analogize this to perishing (halak), requiring the guarantor to pay the value at the time of change.

The author notes that qiyas is continuous and cannot be exhausted; these examples illustrate its scope. The footnote clarifies the term 'fuduli' and the hadith source for the liability rule.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Applying the ruling of a textual case to a new case due to shared cause ('illa).
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies the ruling and is common to both original and new case.
الوكالة العامة (al-wikala al-'amma): A contract of agency where the delegated tasks are not specified individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analogy regarding the usurper (ghasib), what legal effect does transforming the usurped item (e.g., steel into a sword) have?
A) The usurper must return the original item unchanged.
B) The transformation is treated like perishing (halak), requiring the usurper to pay the value.
C) The usurper becomes owner of the new item if it is transformed.
D) The owner has no further claim after transformation.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas allows the mufti to extend rulings to new cases based on a shared 'illa, provided the 'illa is valid and not overridden by a stronger source.

Qiyas Example 1: Silence as Consent in Marriage Contracts
Illustrates qiyas via the silence-example from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply qiyas by identifying the asl, illa, and far' in the hadith about a virgin's silence and extending the ruling to contract ratification after unauthorized marriage.

Core Idea
Shyness makes silence a valid consent; the same illa extends to ratification after the fact.

The Prophet ﷺ declared that a virgin's silence is her consent due to shyness. Jurists analogized this to a case where a guardian marries her without permission and she later remains silent—that silence is taken as ratification. This lesson walks through the qiyas structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
The hadith states that when a guardian seeks a virgin's permission for marriage and she remains silent, it counts as consent. This is the established ruling.
The asl is the scenario of seeking permission before the contract.
2
Determine the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the customary shyness that prevents the virgin from verbalizing consent. The text mentions 'al-khajal' (shyness) and 'al-dalalah al-urfiyyah' (customary indication).
Hanafis treat this illa as 'munasib' (appropriate) for qiyas.
3
Identify the new case (far')
The far' is when the guardian marries her without prior permission (as a fuduli), and she learns of the contract later and remains silent.
The far' shares the same illa: shyness prevents objection.
4
Apply the ruling to the new case
Just as silence at the time of permission indicates consent, silence after the contract indicates ratification. The jurists extended the ruling from asl to far'.
This creates a new ruling: post-contract silence = ratification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
۸ - ورد في الحديث النبوي بشأن التوكيل في عقد النكاح أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال عن الفتاة البكر البالغة: «إذنها صُماتها». أي إنها إذا استأذنها وليها بعقد نكاحها فسكتت يعتبر سكوتها توكيلاً، بمقتضى الدلالة العرفية، لأنها يغلب عليها في هذا المقام الخجل عادة. فقاس الفقهاء عليه ما لو زوجها وليها فضولاً دون استثمارها - أي استئذانها - ثم بلغها الخبر فسكتت فاعتبر الفقهاء سكوتها بعد العقد إجازة منها دلالة عرفية، كما اعتُبِرَ سكوتها عند استثمارها إذناً منها.
۹ - ثبت في السنة تجويز اشتراط الخيار للمشتري في عقد البيع، أي اشتراط حق الفسخ أو الإبرام خلال مدة معينة ويسمى: خيار الشرط، لأنَّ المشتري قد يحتاج إلى التروي خشية الغبن فقد شكا أحد الصحابة، وهو بن منقذ، إلى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كثيراً ما يغبن في البيوع، فأرشده إلى اشتراط الخيار بقوله: إذا بايعت فقل: لا خلابة، ولي الخيار ثلاثة أيام. فقاس عليه الفقهاء جواز اشتراط الخيار المذكور للبائع أيضاً لأن حاجته إلى ذلك كحاجة المشتري. وقاسوا أيضاً على أصل خيار الشرط في الجواز حالة أخرى سموها: خيار النقد، وهو أن يشترط البائع على المشتري المستمهل في دفع الثمن أنه إن لم يحضر الثمن خلال مدة معينة فلا بيع بينهما، وذلك خوفاً من أن يغيب المشتري طويلاً ويتأخر في الدفع، وقد أصبح المبيع ملكاً له بالعقد لا يستطيع البائع التصرُّفَ فيه فيتضرر البائع ويبقى معلقاً تحت رحمة المشتري. فبهذا الشرط يحتاط لنفسه. ووجه قياسه على خيار الشرط أن في كليهما شرطاً يقتضي فسخ البيع بعد انعقاده دفعاً لحاجة مشروعة. (ر) الدرر شرح الغرر ١٥٢/٢). هذه أمثلة قليلة ضربناها للتوضيح تعدُّ غَيْضاً من فيض من وقائع القياس في الفقه الإسلامي، فإنَّ معظم الأحكام الفقهية في النوازل الجديدة إنما ثَبَت ويثبت بطريق القياس.
٨/٣ - مما تقدم يتضح ما للقياس من شأن عظيم في إثبات الأحكام واستنباطها. فهو طريق ضروري هام لتوسيع دائرة النصوص المحدودة حتى تشمل ما لا يتناهى من الحوادث الجديدة. ولا يغني عن القياس العموم في عبارة النص العام. لأنَّ النص العام إنما يشمل عمومه جميع الأفراد الداخلة في مفهومه فقط. أما القياس فإنه يجعل النصوص - حتى الخاصة منها ـ شاملة لما لا يدخل في مفهومها من أنواع الحوادث وأفرادها وذلك بطريق الإلحاق للتشابه في العلة، فيضيف إلى مجموعة النصوص التشريعية الأصلية نصوصاً فقهية للعلماء المستنبطين لا تقف عند حد، وهي قائمة على أسس تلك النصوص الأصلية وقواعدها. ثم إن تلك الأحكام الفرعية التي تثبت بطريق الاستنباط والقياس تصبح أصولاً للقياس يقاس عليها غيرها مما يشابهها في العلل، وهكذا إلى
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. 8 - It is reported in the prophetic hadith concerning appointment of an agent in the marriage contract that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding the virgin adult girl: 'Her consent is her silence.' That is, if her guardian seeks her permission for her marriage contract and she remains silent, her silence is considered an appointment of agency, by virtue of customary indication, because shyness usually overcomes her in this situation. The jurists analogized from this the case where her guardian marries her as a unauthorized agent without consulting her – i.e., seeking her permission – then news reaches her and she remains silent; the jurists considered her silence after the contract as a ratification by customary indication, just as her silence at the time of seeking permission was considered permission from her. 9 - It is established in the Sunnah to permit stipulating an option for the buyer in the sale contract, i.e., stipulating the right of rescission or confirmation during a specified period, called: option of condition (khiyar al-shart), because the buyer may need to deliberate for fear of being cheated. One of the Companions, Habban ibn Munqidh, complained to the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he was often cheated in transactions, so he guided him to stipulate the option by saying: 'When you make a sale, say: no cheating, and I have the option for three days.' The jurists analogized from this the permissibility of stipulating the mentioned option also for the seller, because his need for that is like the buyer's need. They also analogized from the original permissibility of option of condition another case they called: option of cash payment (khiyar al-naqd), which is that the seller stipulates on the buyer who is given time to pay the price that if he does not bring the price within a specified period, then there is no sale between them, out of fear that the buyer might be absent for a long time and delay payment, while the sold item has become his property by the contract and the seller cannot dispose of it, so the seller is harmed and remains suspended at the mercy of the buyer. By this condition, he protects himself. The basis of analogy to option of condition is that in both there is a condition that necessitates rescission of the sale after its conclusion to fulfill a legitimate need. (See: al-Durar Sharh al-Ghurrar 2/152). These are a few examples we have given for illustration, a drop from the ocean of instances of qiyas in Islamic jurisprudence; indeed, most of the juristic rulings on new incidents are established and continue to be established by way of qiyas. 8/3 - From the foregoing, the great significance of qiyas in establishing and deriving rulings becomes clear. It is an essential important method to expand the scope of limited texts so that they encompass the infinite new events. The generality in the wording of a general text does not suffice instead of qiyas. Because a general text only includes all individuals falling within its concept. As for qiyas, it makes texts – even specific ones – inclusive of types of events and individuals not entering their concept, by way of attachment due to similarity in the ratio legis, thus adding to the original legislative texts an unlimited set of juristic texts derived by the scholars, which are based on those original texts and their rules. Then those branch rulings established by derivation and qiyas become principles for qiyas, so that other similar cases are analogized to them, and so on.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on sources of Islamic jurisprudence, specifically demonstrating the application of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, presents two concrete examples from the Sunnah where the Prophet’s words were used as a basis for analogy. Example 8: The hadith stating a virgin’s silence is her consent. The jurists extended this to a similar situation where a guardian marries the girl without prior permission, and her subsequent silence is taken as ratification. This shows how the underlying rationale (illa) – the shyness that makes silence a reliable indicator of consent – applies equally to both cases. Example 9: The hadith allowing a buyer to stipulate an option (khiyar al-shart) to avoid being cheated. Jurists analogized to allow the seller to stipulate the same option, and also developed a new type called khiyar al-naqd (option of cash payment) to protect the seller from delayed payment. The common illa is the need to prevent harm (ghabn or delay). The author then emphasizes the critical role of qiyas in expanding the limited number of revealed texts to cover countless new situations, noting that general texts alone cannot cover every specific case because they are limited to their literal meanings. Qiyas works by identifying the effective cause (illa) in an original ruling and applying it to a new case. Moreover, the derived rulings themselves become precedents for further analogies, creating a dynamic system of legal reasoning. This is a hallmark of Hanafi methodology, where qiyas is a primary tool for legal development, especially in matters of mu'amalat (transactions).

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illa).
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause or rationale behind a legal ruling, serving as the basis for analogical extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the underlying reason (illa) for considering a virgin's silence as consent in the hadith, and to which other case did jurists extend this?
A) Shyness; extended to post-contract silence as ratification.
B) Lack of consent; extended to forced marriage.
C) Customary practice; extended to all contracts.
D) The guardian's authority; extended to maternal guardians.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas extends a ruling from a known case to a new case when the underlying cause (illa) is present, even if the new case occurs after the contract.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

Qiyas Example 2: Extending Khiyar al-Shart to Seller and to Cash Option
Demonstrates qiyas through khiyar examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply qiyas to extend khiyar al-shart to the seller and to derive khiyar al-naqd, identifying the shared illa.

Core Idea
The need to avoid harm justifies extending the option to both parties and to cash payment conditions.

The Prophet ﷺ allowed a buyer to stipulate a three-day option to avoid being cheated. Jurists used qiyas to grant the same option to the seller and created a new 'cash option' (khiyar al-naqd) to protect the seller from delayed payment. This lesson traces the analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl) and its ruling
The hadith allows the buyer to stipulate 'khiyar al-shart' for three days to prevent being cheated. This is the established ruling.
The asl is the buyer's option from the Sunnah.
2
Determine the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the need to avoid harm (defrauding or delay) and to ensure fairness. The buyer's need to deliberate due to fear of being cheated is the trigger.
Hanafis see the illa as hifz al-maslahah (protecting interest).
3
First extension: option for the seller
Jurists reasoned that the seller's need to avoid harm is similar (e.g., buyer delaying payment). So they extended the option to the seller via qiyas.
The far' is the seller stipulating the same option.
4
Second extension: option of cash payment (khiyar al-naqd)
The seller may stipulate that if the buyer does not pay within a specified time, the sale is void. This is analogized from khiyar al-shart because both involve a condition that rescinds the contract to fulfill a legitimate need.
The illa is the same: need to avoid harm from non-payment.

Source Text

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a contract allowing either party to rescind or confirm the contract within a specified period.
خيار النقد (khiyar al-naqd): Option of cash payment: a condition in a sale that if the buyer does not pay within a specified time, the sale is void.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).

What is the common illa between khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-naqd?
A) Preventing fraud
B) Need to avoid harm and fulfill legitimate need
C) Buyer's right to inspect goods

Key Takeaway
Qiyas can extend a single hadith to multiple new cases when the illa is common, generating new types of contracts.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
