The Role of Qiyas in Expanding Legal Texts
Explains the necessity and function of qiyas in fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qiyas is necessary to extend the limited number of revealed texts to infinite new cases, and distinguish qiyas from the generality of a text (umum).

Core Idea
Qiyas makes even specific texts cover new cases by analogy, surpassing the limitation of general wording.

The author concludes that qiyas is indispensable for expanding the reach of the Quran and Sunnah. While a general text covers only what its wording includes, qiyas attaches new cases to existing rulings through a shared cause, creating an unlimited system of fiqh. This lesson clarifies the unique role of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the limitation of general texts (umum)
A general text (e.g., 'do not cheat') includes all instances that fall under its concept, but not cases that fall outside its wording even if they share the same rationale.
The author states: 'al-nass al-amm innama yashmilu jami' al-afrad al-dakhilah fi mafhumihi faqat'.
2
Understand qiyas as an extension beyond wording
Qiyas makes texts (even specific ones) include cases not within their literal meaning by 'ilhāq' (attaching) due to similarity in illa.
This is the core of qiyas: it goes beyond the lexical scope.
3
Realize the generative nature of qiyas
The derived rulings become new 'asl' for further qiyas, creating an ever-expanding network of fiqh rulings.
The text says: 'thumma inna tilka al-ahkam al-far'iyyah... tusbihu usulan li al-qiyas'.
4
Contrast qiyas with textual interpretation
Textual interpretation (tafsir) clarifies what the words mean; qiyas adds new cases that the words do not literally cover.
This distinguishes qiyas from istinbat from the text itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
۸ - ورد في الحديث النبوي بشأن التوكيل في عقد النكاح أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال عن الفتاة البكر البالغة: «إذنها صُماتها». أي إنها إذا استأذنها وليها بعقد نكاحها فسكتت يعتبر سكوتها توكيلاً، بمقتضى الدلالة العرفية، لأنها يغلب عليها في هذا المقام الخجل عادة. فقاس الفقهاء عليه ما لو زوجها وليها فضولاً دون استثمارها - أي استئذانها - ثم بلغها الخبر فسكتت فاعتبر الفقهاء سكوتها بعد العقد إجازة منها دلالة عرفية، كما اعتُبِرَ سكوتها عند استثمارها إذناً منها.
۹ - ثبت في السنة تجويز اشتراط الخيار للمشتري في عقد البيع، أي اشتراط حق الفسخ أو الإبرام خلال مدة معينة ويسمى: خيار الشرط، لأنَّ المشتري قد يحتاج إلى التروي خشية الغبن فقد شكا أحد الصحابة، وهو بن منقذ، إلى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كثيراً ما يغبن في البيوع، فأرشده إلى اشتراط الخيار بقوله: إذا بايعت فقل: لا خلابة، ولي الخيار ثلاثة أيام. فقاس عليه الفقهاء جواز اشتراط الخيار المذكور للبائع أيضاً لأن حاجته إلى ذلك كحاجة المشتري. وقاسوا أيضاً على أصل خيار الشرط في الجواز حالة أخرى سموها: خيار النقد، وهو أن يشترط البائع على المشتري المستمهل في دفع الثمن أنه إن لم يحضر الثمن خلال مدة معينة فلا بيع بينهما، وذلك خوفاً من أن يغيب المشتري طويلاً ويتأخر في الدفع، وقد أصبح المبيع ملكاً له بالعقد لا يستطيع البائع التصرُّفَ فيه فيتضرر البائع ويبقى معلقاً تحت رحمة المشتري. فبهذا الشرط يحتاط لنفسه. ووجه قياسه على خيار الشرط أن في كليهما شرطاً يقتضي فسخ البيع بعد انعقاده دفعاً لحاجة مشروعة. (ر) الدرر شرح الغرر ١٥٢/٢). هذه أمثلة قليلة ضربناها للتوضيح تعدُّ غَيْضاً من فيض من وقائع القياس في الفقه الإسلامي، فإنَّ معظم الأحكام الفقهية في النوازل الجديدة إنما ثَبَت ويثبت بطريق القياس.
٨/٣ - مما تقدم يتضح ما للقياس من شأن عظيم في إثبات الأحكام واستنباطها. فهو طريق ضروري هام لتوسيع دائرة النصوص المحدودة حتى تشمل ما لا يتناهى من الحوادث الجديدة. ولا يغني عن القياس العموم في عبارة النص العام. لأنَّ النص العام إنما يشمل عمومه جميع الأفراد الداخلة في مفهومه فقط. أما القياس فإنه يجعل النصوص - حتى الخاصة منها ـ شاملة لما لا يدخل في مفهومها من أنواع الحوادث وأفرادها وذلك بطريق الإلحاق للتشابه في العلة، فيضيف إلى مجموعة النصوص التشريعية الأصلية نصوصاً فقهية للعلماء المستنبطين لا تقف عند حد، وهي قائمة على أسس تلك النصوص الأصلية وقواعدها. ثم إن تلك الأحكام الفرعية التي تثبت بطريق الاستنباط والقياس تصبح أصولاً للقياس يقاس عليها غيرها مما يشابهها في العلل، وهكذا إلى
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. 8 - It is reported in the prophetic hadith concerning appointment of an agent in the marriage contract that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding the virgin adult girl: 'Her consent is her silence.' That is, if her guardian seeks her permission for her marriage contract and she remains silent, her silence is considered an appointment of agency, by virtue of customary indication, because shyness usually overcomes her in this situation. The jurists analogized from this the case where her guardian marries her as a unauthorized agent without consulting her – i.e., seeking her permission – then news reaches her and she remains silent; the jurists considered her silence after the contract as a ratification by customary indication, just as her silence at the time of seeking permission was considered permission from her. 9 - It is established in the Sunnah to permit stipulating an option for the buyer in the sale contract, i.e., stipulating the right of rescission or confirmation during a specified period, called: option of condition (khiyar al-shart), because the buyer may need to deliberate for fear of being cheated. One of the Companions, Habban ibn Munqidh, complained to the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he was often cheated in transactions, so he guided him to stipulate the option by saying: 'When you make a sale, say: no cheating, and I have the option for three days.' The jurists analogized from this the permissibility of stipulating the mentioned option also for the seller, because his need for that is like the buyer's need. They also analogized from the original permissibility of option of condition another case they called: option of cash payment (khiyar al-naqd), which is that the seller stipulates on the buyer who is given time to pay the price that if he does not bring the price within a specified period, then there is no sale between them, out of fear that the buyer might be absent for a long time and delay payment, while the sold item has become his property by the contract and the seller cannot dispose of it, so the seller is harmed and remains suspended at the mercy of the buyer. By this condition, he protects himself. The basis of analogy to option of condition is that in both there is a condition that necessitates rescission of the sale after its conclusion to fulfill a legitimate need. (See: al-Durar Sharh al-Ghurrar 2/152). These are a few examples we have given for illustration, a drop from the ocean of instances of qiyas in Islamic jurisprudence; indeed, most of the juristic rulings on new incidents are established and continue to be established by way of qiyas. 8/3 - From the foregoing, the great significance of qiyas in establishing and deriving rulings becomes clear. It is an essential important method to expand the scope of limited texts so that they encompass the infinite new events. The generality in the wording of a general text does not suffice instead of qiyas. Because a general text only includes all individuals falling within its concept. As for qiyas, it makes texts – even specific ones – inclusive of types of events and individuals not entering their concept, by way of attachment due to similarity in the ratio legis, thus adding to the original legislative texts an unlimited set of juristic texts derived by the scholars, which are based on those original texts and their rules. Then those branch rulings established by derivation and qiyas become principles for qiyas, so that other similar cases are analogized to them, and so on.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on sources of Islamic jurisprudence, specifically demonstrating the application of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, presents two concrete examples from the Sunnah where the Prophet’s words were used as a basis for analogy. Example 8: The hadith stating a virgin’s silence is her consent. The jurists extended this to a similar situation where a guardian marries the girl without prior permission, and her subsequent silence is taken as ratification. This shows how the underlying rationale (illa) – the shyness that makes silence a reliable indicator of consent – applies equally to both cases. Example 9: The hadith allowing a buyer to stipulate an option (khiyar al-shart) to avoid being cheated. Jurists analogized to allow the seller to stipulate the same option, and also developed a new type called khiyar al-naqd (option of cash payment) to protect the seller from delayed payment. The common illa is the need to prevent harm (ghabn or delay). The author then emphasizes the critical role of qiyas in expanding the limited number of revealed texts to cover countless new situations, noting that general texts alone cannot cover every specific case because they are limited to their literal meanings. Qiyas works by identifying the effective cause (illa) in an original ruling and applying it to a new case. Moreover, the derived rulings themselves become precedents for further analogies, creating a dynamic system of legal reasoning. This is a hallmark of Hanafi methodology, where qiyas is a primary tool for legal development, especially in matters of mu'amalat (transactions).

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illa).
النص العام (al-nass al-amm): A general text that applies to all individuals falling under its linguistic concept.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does qiyas achieve that a general text cannot?
A) It clarifies ambiguous words.
B) It makes texts inclusive of cases not within their concept.
C) It abrogates previous rulings.
D) It provides a literal meaning.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is essential to expand the limited number of revealed texts to cover unlimited new cases, and it creates a dynamic system where derived rulings become new sources for further qiyas.

Defining Istihsan: Judicial Preference as a Subsidiary Source
Defining istihsan and its subsidiary role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam al-Karkhi's definition of istihsan and explain its role as a subsidiary source of Islamic law.

Core Idea
Istihsan is turning from apparent analogy to a stronger evidence, not arbitrary preference.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of istihsan as defined by the Hanafi school. Istihsan is one of the subsidiary sources of Islamic law, and it plays a crucial role in Hanafi methodology. Understanding its definition and classification is essential for any mufti working within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subsidiary sources
The passage lists three subsidiary sources: istihsan, istislah, and custom. Recognize that these are derived from the four primary sources.
2
Memorize al-Karkhi's definition
Al-Karkhi defines istihsan as 'turning away from the ruling of its analogues to another ruling, due to a stronger reason.' Note the key elements: 'turning away' (عدول), 'from analogues' (عن حكم نظائرها), 'to another ruling' (إلى حكم آخر), 'stronger reason' (لوجه أقوى).
3
Contrast with apparent analogy
Apparent analogy links a case to its analogues; istihsan detaches it. The 'stronger reason' can be a hidden analogy, text, consensus, or necessity.
4
Classify istihsan as subsidiary
Istihsan is not an independent source; it returns to the primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas). Most scholars consider it a subset of these.

ومعنى ذلك أن الاستحسان هو عدول عن حكم القياس في المسألة إلى حكم آخر لسبب يقتضي هذا العدول فإن الاستحسان هو قطع المسألة عن نظائرها القياسية، فهو عكس القياس الظاهر الذي هو : إلحاق المسألة بنظائرها في الحكم. وبناء على نوع العلة التي تقطع لأجلها المسألة الاستحسانية عن نظائرها القياسية ينقسم الاستحسان إلى نوعين الاستحسان القياسي واستحسان الضرورة(١).

٣/٤ ـ فأما الاستحسان القياسي فهو أن يعدل بالمسألة عن حكم القياس الظاهر المتبادر فيها إلى حكم مغاير بقياس آخر هو أدق وأخفى من الأول، ولكنه أقوى حجة، وأسد نظراً، وأصحُ استنتاجاً منه . ولشيوع هذا النوع من الاستحسان كثيراً في طريقة فقهاء الحنفية قد يقتصر بعضهم على تعريف الاستحسان على أنه هو «القياس الخفي» وهذا النوع من الاستحسان في الحقيقة إنما هو ترجيح لأحد الأقيسة عند تعدد وجوه القياس وتعارضها في المسألة الواحدة، فهو من القياس وإليه .

Chapter Four: Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan
1/4 - There are other shar'i bases for proving fiqh rulings besides the four basic sources mentioned earlier. The texts of the Book and Sunnah indicate that they are considered valid grounds for proving rulings.
However, these sources are in reality subsidiary and branched from the four basic sources. Therefore, most scholars did not consider them additional but rather regarded them as returning to them.
The most important of these subsidiary sources are three, which we will explain in this chapter and the two following chapters:
- Istihsan
- Istislah, or the principle of unrestricted interests
- Custom

First Section: Istihsan
2/4 - Istihsan is turning away from a case from the ruling of its analogues to another ruling, due to a stronger reason that necessitates this turning away.
This is how Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, one of the Hanafi imams, defines it. Perhaps it is the best transmitted definition of istihsan and the most comprehensive of its types as will be explained (see Kashf al-Asrar Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi, 3/4, and the book 'Abu Hanifah' by Professor Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra, Part Two, p. 174).

Book Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
And that means that istihsan is turning away from the ruling of analogy in a case to another ruling due to a reason that necessitates this turning away. Thus istihsan is detaching the case from its analogical counterparts, and it is the opposite of apparent analogy, which is attaching the case to its analogues in ruling. Based on the type of cause for which the istihsani case is detached from its analogical counterparts, istihsan is divided into two types: analogical istihsan and necessity istihsan (1).

First Subsection: Analogical Istihsan
3/4 - As for analogical istihsan, it is turning away from the ruling of the apparent, readily apparent analogy in a case to a different ruling by another analogy that is more subtle and hidden than the first, but stronger in argument, sounder in reasoning, and more correct in deduction. Due to the prevalence of this type of istihsan in the method of Hanafi jurists, some may restrict the definition of istihsan to being 'hidden analogy'. This type of istihsan is in reality a preference for one of the analogies when there are multiple aspects of analogy and they conflict in a single case. So it is from analogy and belongs to it.

4/4 - Examples of Analogical Istihsan:
Among the examples of analogical istihsan are the following cases:
1 - Joint debt (2): if one of the creditors receives the amount of his share...
(1) Usuli scholars among the Hanafis divide istihsan into four types, adding two more: istihsan based on Sunnah and istihsan based on consensus. We will critique that at the end of the research (section 8/4).
(2) Joint debt is that which is established for two or more persons in the liability of a third person due to a single cause, such as something owned by two persons equally if they sell it as a single transaction for a deferred price. Then its price becomes a joint debt owed by the buyer to both. Similarly, if they did not sell it but a third person destroyed it, he guarantees its value due to destruction, and this value becomes a joint debt for both against the destroyer. If the cause of the debt is not single, it is not a joint debt, as when a person borrows two loans from two persons, each loan by a separate contract.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aamm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa introduces the concept of istihsan as one of the subsidiary sources of Islamic jurisprudence. The author begins by stating that besides the four primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas), there are other valid Shar'i bases for deriving rulings, but they are subsidiary and ultimately return to the primary sources. The three most important subsidiary sources are istihsan, istislah (masalih mursala), and custom ('urf). The focus of this section is istihsan.

The definition of istihsan according to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi scholar, is 'turning away from the ruling of its analogues to another ruling due to a stronger reason.' This means that in a particular case, the jurist abandons the ruling that would normally be given by apparent analogy (qiyas jali) in favor of a different ruling because there is a stronger evidence or reason that justifies this departure. Istihsan is thus the opposite of apparent analogy: whereas analogy links a case to its analogues, istihsan detaches it from them.

Based on the nature of the cause ('illa) that necessitates the departure, istihsan is divided into two main types: analogical istihsan (istihsan qiyasi) and necessity istihsan (istihsan daruri). The text focuses on analogical istihsan, which is a preference for a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over an apparent analogy. In other words, when there are conflicting analogies for a single case, the jurist chooses the hidden analogy that is stronger in argument, reasoning, and deduction. This type of istihsan is essentially a form of analogy itself, as it involves weighing and preferring one analogical reasoning over another.

The example provided, though incomplete in this excerpt, is about a joint debt: if one creditor collects his share from the debtor, the ruling under apparent analogy might differ from the ruling under istihsan. The footnote explains that joint debt is a debt owed to two or more creditors from a single cause, such as a joint sale. The istihsan ruling would be that the creditor who collects his share does not nullify the rights of the other creditor, contrary to what apparent analogy might suggest.

It is worth noting that some Hanafi usulis divide istihsan into four types, adding istihsan based on Sunnah and istihsan based on consensus, but the author critiques this classification later. For now, the bipartite division is presented as fundamental.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): العدول بالمسألة عن حكم نظائرها إلى حكم آخر لوجه أقوى يقتضي هذا العدول (تعريف الكرخي)
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): قياس أدق وأخفى من القياس الظاهر لكنه أقوى حجة وأسد نظراً
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): ما ثبت لاثنين فأكثر في ذمة ثالث بسبب متحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is the preference of a stronger evidence over apparent analogy, a key tool in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Analogical Istihsan: The Hidden Analogy (Qiyas Khafi)
Explaining analogical istihsan as hidden analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define analogical istihsan and identify it as a preference for hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over apparent analogy (qiyas jali).

Core Idea
Analogical istihsan is not abandoning analogy but preferring a stronger hidden analogy over a weaker apparent one.

Analogical istihsan (istihsan qiyasi) is the most common type of istihsan in Hanafi jurisprudence. It occurs when a jurist prefers a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over an apparent analogy (qiyas jali) because the hidden one is stronger in reasoning and evidence. This lesson explores how this process works and provides a concrete example from the text.

Guided Path
1
Define analogical istihsan
Analogical istihsan is turning away from the ruling of apparent analogy to a different ruling based on another analogy that is more subtle and stronger.
2
Distinguish apparent vs. hidden analogy
Apparent analogy (qiyas jali) is the immediate analogy that comes to mind. Hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) is more subtle but has stronger evidence.
3
Understand the preference process
When multiple analogies conflict, the jurist weighs them and prefers the one with stronger argumentation. This preference is analogical istihsan.
4
Apply to the joint debt example
In joint debt, apparent analogy might suggest that if one creditor collects his share, the debt is reduced proportionally for all. But hidden analogy considers the separate nature of each creditor's right, allowing the collection without prejudice.

هذا ما يعرفه به الإمام أبو الحسن الكرخي من أئمة المذهب الحنفي. ولعله أفضل التعاريف المأثورة للاستحسان وأشملها لأنواعه الآتي بيانها (ر كشف الأسرار شرح أصول البزدوي ، ٣/٤، وكتاب «أبو حنيفة» للأستاذ الشيخ محمد أبي زهرة القسم الثاني، ف/ ١٧٤).

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
ومعنى ذلك أن الاستحسان هو عدول عن حكم القياس في المسألة إلى حكم آخر لسبب يقتضي هذا العدول فإن الاستحسان هو قطع المسألة عن نظائرها القياسية، فهو عكس القياس الظاهر الذي هو : إلحاق المسألة بنظائرها في الحكم. وبناء على نوع العلة التي تقطع لأجلها المسألة الاستحسانية عن نظائرها القياسية ينقسم الاستحسان إلى نوعين الاستحسان القياسي واستحسان الضرورة(١).
المطلب الأول: الاستحسان القياسي
٣/٤ ـ فأما الاستحسان القياسي فهو أن يعدل بالمسألة عن حكم القياس الظاهر المتبادر فيها إلى حكم مغاير بقياس آخر هو أدق وأخفى من الأول، ولكنه أقوى حجة، وأسد نظراً، وأصحُ استنتاجاً منه . ولشيوع هذا النوع من الاستحسان كثيراً في طريقة فقهاء الحنفية قد يقتصر بعضهم على تعريف الاستحسان على أنه هو «القياس الخفي» وهذا النوع من الاستحسان في الحقيقة إنما هو ترجيح لأحد الأقيسة عند تعدد وجوه القياس وتعارضها في المسألة الواحدة، فهو من القياس وإليه .
٤/٤ - أمثلة الاستحسان القياسي :
ومن أمثلة الاستحسان القياسي المسائل التالية :
۱ - إِنَّ الدِّين المشترك (۲) إذا قبض منه أحد الدائنين مقدار حصته لا
(۱) بقسم علماء الأصول من الحنفية الاستحسان إلى أربعة أنواع، فيزيدون نوعين هما: استحسان السنة، واستحسان الإجماع. وسننتقد ذلك آخر البحث (ف ٨/٤).
(۲) الدين المُشْتَرك هو ما ثبت لاثنين فأكثر في ذمة ثالث بسبب متحد، كشيء يملكه شخصان مناصفة بينهما إذا باعاه صفقة واحدة بثمن مؤجل، فثمنه يكون ديناً مشتركاً لهما على المشتري وكذا لو لم يبيعاه بيعاً بل أتلفه شخص ثالث، فإنه يضمن قيمته بسبب الإتلاف، وتكون هذه القيمة ديناً مشتركاً لهما على المتلف.
فلو لم يكن سبب الدين واحداً لا يكون ديناً مشتركاً، كما لو اقترض شخص قَرْضَين من شخصين كل قرض بعقد على حدة.
Chapter Four: Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan
1/4 - There are other shar'i bases for proving fiqh rulings besides the four basic sources mentioned earlier. The texts of the Book and Sunnah indicate that they are considered valid grounds for proving rulings.
However, these sources are in reality subsidiary and branched from the four basic sources. Therefore, most scholars did not consider them additional but rather regarded them as returning to them.
The most important of these subsidiary sources are three, which we will explain in this chapter and the two following chapters:
- Istihsan
- Istislah, or the principle of unrestricted interests
- Custom

First Section: Istihsan
2/4 - Istihsan is turning away from a case from the ruling of its analogues to another ruling, due to a stronger reason that necessitates this turning away.
This is how Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, one of the Hanafi imams, defines it. Perhaps it is the best transmitted definition of istihsan and the most comprehensive of its types as will be explained (see Kashf al-Asrar Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi, 3/4, and the book 'Abu Hanifah' by Professor Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra, Part Two, p. 174).

Book Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
And that means that istihsan is turning away from the ruling of analogy in a case to another ruling due to a reason that necessitates this turning away. Thus istihsan is detaching the case from its analogical counterparts, and it is the opposite of apparent analogy, which is attaching the case to its analogues in ruling. Based on the type of cause for which the istihsani case is detached from its analogical counterparts, istihsan is divided into two types: analogical istihsan and necessity istihsan (1).

First Subsection: Analogical Istihsan
3/4 - As for analogical istihsan, it is turning away from the ruling of the apparent, readily apparent analogy in a case to a different ruling by another analogy that is more subtle and hidden than the first, but stronger in argument, sounder in reasoning, and more correct in deduction. Due to the prevalence of this type of istihsan in the method of Hanafi jurists, some may restrict the definition of istihsan to being 'hidden analogy'. This type of istihsan is in reality a preference for one of the analogies when there are multiple aspects of analogy and they conflict in a single case. So it is from analogy and belongs to it.

4/4 - Examples of Analogical Istihsan:
Among the examples of analogical istihsan are the following cases:
1 - Joint debt (2): if one of the creditors receives the amount of his share...
(1) Usuli scholars among the Hanafis divide istihsan into four types, adding two more: istihsan based on Sunnah and istihsan based on consensus. We will critique that at the end of the research (section 8/4).
(2) Joint debt is that which is established for two or more persons in the liability of a third person due to a single cause, such as something owned by two persons equally if they sell it as a single transaction for a deferred price. Then its price becomes a joint debt owed by the buyer to both. Similarly, if they did not sell it but a third person destroyed it, he guarantees its value due to destruction, and this value becomes a joint debt for both against the destroyer. If the cause of the debt is not single, it is not a joint debt, as when a person borrows two loans from two persons, each loan by a separate contract.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aamm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa introduces the concept of istihsan as one of the subsidiary sources of Islamic jurisprudence. The author begins by stating that besides the four primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas), there are other valid Shar'i bases for deriving rulings, but they are subsidiary and ultimately return to the primary sources. The three most important subsidiary sources are istihsan, istislah (masalih mursala), and custom ('urf). The focus of this section is istihsan.

The definition of istihsan according to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi scholar, is 'turning away from the ruling of its analogues to another ruling due to a stronger reason.' This means that in a particular case, the jurist abandons the ruling that would normally be given by apparent analogy (qiyas jali) in favor of a different ruling because there is a stronger evidence or reason that justifies this departure. Istihsan is thus the opposite of apparent analogy: whereas analogy links a case to its analogues, istihsan detaches it from them.

Based on the nature of the cause ('illa) that necessitates the departure, istihsan is divided into two main types: analogical istihsan (istihsan qiyasi) and necessity istihsan (istihsan daruri). The text focuses on analogical istihsan, which is a preference for a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) over an apparent analogy. In other words, when there are conflicting analogies for a single case, the jurist chooses the hidden analogy that is stronger in argument, reasoning, and deduction. This type of istihsan is essentially a form of analogy itself, as it involves weighing and preferring one analogical reasoning over another.

The example provided, though incomplete in this excerpt, is about a joint debt: if one creditor collects his share from the debtor, the ruling under apparent analogy might differ from the ruling under istihsan. The footnote explains that joint debt is a debt owed to two or more creditors from a single cause, such as a joint sale. The istihsan ruling would be that the creditor who collects his share does not nullify the rights of the other creditor, contrary to what apparent analogy might suggest.

It is worth noting that some Hanafi usulis divide istihsan into four types, adding istihsan based on Sunnah and istihsan based on consensus, but the author critiques this classification later. For now, the bipartite division is presented as fundamental.

Key Terms
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): قياس أدق وأخفى من القياس الظاهر لكنه أقوى حجة وأسد نظراً
القياس الظاهر (al-qiyas al-jali): القياس البادي المتبادر للذهن
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): ما ثبت لاثنين فأكثر في ذمة ثالث بسبب متحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It completely rejects analogy in favor of custom.

Key Takeaway
Analogical istihsan is a method of preferring the stronger hidden analogy over the weaker apparent one, remaining within the framework of qiyas.

Istihsan Qiyasi: Definition and Classification
Definition and classification of istihsan qiyasi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihsan qiyasi, distinguish it from manifest qiyas, and identify its place within Hanafi legal methodology as a preference between conflicting analogies.

Core Idea
Istihsan qiyasi is preferring a hidden but stronger analogy over the manifest one — it is a tarjih between conflicting qiyas.

In the Hanafi school, istihsan is a secondary source of law that often involves choosing a more subtle analogy over a surface-level one. This lesson unpacks the definition of istihsan qiyasi, its relationship to manifest qiyas, and its classification based on the cause (illa) for departing from the apparent analogy.

Guided Path
1
Define istihsan conceptually
Start with the general definition: istihsan is turning away from the ruling of qiyas in a case to another ruling due to a reason that necessitates this turning. Note that it is the opposite of manifest qiyas, which attaches the case to its counterparts.
2
Identify the reason for departure
Analyze the 'reason' (sabab) in the definition. The reason is the existence of a stronger but hidden analogy (qiyas khafi). This hidden analogy is subtler and more penetrating than the manifest qiyas.
3
Distinguish istihsan from manifest qiyas
Manifest qiyas attaches a case to its nazair (counterparts) in ruling. Istihsan detaches the case from those nazair. The detaching is justified by a stronger analogy that points to a different ruling.
4
Explain classification into two types
Based on the type of cause (illa) for the detachment, istihsan divides into istihsan qiyasi (analogical) and istihsan al-darura (necessity). Focus on qiyasi, which is a tarjih (preference) among conflicting analogies.
5
Understand the Hanafi-specific view
Some Hanafi jurists define istihsan simply as 'hidden qiyas' because this type is so prevalent. The istihsan qiyasi is essentially a preference (tarjih) for one qiyas over another when multiple analogies conflict.

Source Text

And the meaning of that is that istihsan is turning away from the ruling of qiyas in a case to another ruling due to a reason that necessitates this turning. Indeed, istihsan is detaching the case from its analogical counterparts. It is the opposite of manifest qiyas, which is: attaching the case to its counterparts in ruling. Based on the type of cause (illa) for which the istihsani case is detached from its analogical counterparts, istihsan is divided into two types: qiyasi (analogical) istihsan and daruri (necessity) istihsan. (1)
First Request: Istihsan Qiyasi
3/4 - As for istihsan qiyasi, it is that one turns away from the ruling of the manifest, readily apparent qiyas in the case to a different ruling by another qiyas that is subtler and more hidden than the first, but it is stronger in proof, sounder in consideration, and more correct in conclusion. Due to the prevalence of this type of istihsan in the method of Hanafi jurists, some of them restrict the definition of istihsan to being 'hidden qiyas'. This type of istihsan in reality is but a preference for one qiyas over another when there are multiple aspects of qiyas and they conflict in a single case. So it is from qiyas and to it.
4/4 - Examples of Istihsan Qiyasi:
Among the examples of istihsan qiyasi are the following cases:
1 - Indeed, the common debt (2) - if one of the creditors receives the amount of his share, he does not have the right to exclusively keep it; rather, his partner in the debt can demand from him his share of what was received. If what was received perishes in the hand of the receiver before the second partner takes his share from it, the requirement of manifest qiyas would be that it perishes from the account of both, because just as they share the received amount if it remains safe, they should jointly bear the burden of its loss if it perishes. But in istihsan, what perishes in the hand of the receiver is considered perished only from his share, and the share that was not received belongs to the second partner. This is because originally he was not obligated to share with the receiver in what he received; rather, he could leave the received amount to the receiver and pursue the debtor for his share.
2 - It is an established rule that a person is bound by his admission regarding his own rights, not regarding the rights of others. So if, for example, someone admits that he and his brother owe a sum of money, he is liable for his portion of it, but his brother is not liable if he denies. Based on this, if someone claims to be an agent for an absent creditor to collect his debt, and the debtor admits his agency, he is ordered to pay the debt to him based on his admission. And accordingly, if someone deposits something with another and then goes absent, and a person claims to be the agent of the absent one to collect his deposit, and the depositary admits his agency, the requirement of manifest qiyas, based on the case of debt collection, would be to obligate the depositary to hand over the deposit to him. But istihsan dictates not obligating the depositary to hand over the deposit to him, even if the depositary admits his agency, due to the possibility that the owner of the deposit might appear and deny the agency, and his deposit would be gone and perhaps could not be retrieved, and his right is attached to the specific object. Unlike the case of debt, where the right of the creditor is attached to the debtor's liability (dhimma), not to the specific amount that this debtor pays to the supposed agent for collection. If the creditor appears and denies the agency, it becomes clear that the earlier payment was not a valid discharge of the debt, because the agent's agency was not established, so the creditor's right remains as it was in the debtor's liability, and he is required to pay again to the creditor, and he has the right to recourse against the receiver to retrieve what he paid him. So he is ordered to pay again to the one who denied the agency. And the clarification of that is that the process of discharging a debt, in reality and from a juristic perspective, is that...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, explaining istihsan (juristic preference) as a secondary source of Islamic law. It defines istihsan as departing from the ruling of qiyas (analogy) in a case to another ruling due to a stronger reason. Istihsan is essentially detaching the case from its analogical counterparts (nazair), opposite to manifest qiyas which attaches the case to its counterparts. Based on the nature of the cause (illa) justifying the departure, istihsan is divided into two types: istihsan qiyasi (analogical istihsan) and istihsan al-darura (necessity istihsan). The passage then focuses on istihsan qiyasi, which is the most common type in the Hanafi school. It occurs when a case is taken away from the apparent manifest qiyas to a different ruling through another qiyas that is subtler and more hidden but stronger in evidence and reasoning. This type is essentially a preference (tarjih) between conflicting analogies. Some Hanafi scholars even define istihsan as 'hidden qiyas'. The passage then provides two examples. The first example concerns a common debt (dayn mushtarak) owed by one debtor to two creditors. If one creditor receives his share and it is destroyed before the other takes his share, manifest qiyas would require the loss to be shared. But istihsan considers the loss only from the receiver's share because the second creditor was never obligated to share the risk. The second example contrasts two situations: debt vs. deposit. If a person claims to be an agent of an absent creditor and the debtor admits and pays, then if the creditor appears and denies, the debtor must pay again and can seek recourse from the false agent. But in the case of a deposit, if a person claims to be an agent for the absent owner and the depositary admits and delivers the deposit, istihsan protects the depositary from liability because the right is attached to the specific item, unlike debt which is an obligation in the dhimma. So the depositary is not forced to hand over, otherwise the owner might lose his property entirely. These examples illustrate how istihsan qiyasi selects a more nuanced analogy over a superficial one.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): العدول عن حكم القياس في المسألة إلى حكم آخر لسبب يقتضي هذا العدول
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): القياس الأقوى حجة وإن كان أخفى من القياس الظاهر
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): ما ثبت لاثنين فأكثر في ذمة ثالث بسبب متحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Istihsan qiyasi is a preference for a hidden but stronger analogy over a manifest one, making it an integral part of Hanafi analogical reasoning.

Applying Istihsan Qiyasi: The Common Debt and Deposit Examples
Two examples illustrating istihsan qiyasi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the two examples of istihsan qiyasi provided by al-Zarqa, identify the manifest and hidden analogies in each, and explain why the hidden analogy is preferred.

Core Idea
In a common debt, loss from a creditor's share is his alone; in a deposit, the depositary is protected from handing over to a false agent — both examples show hidden qiyas overriding manifest qiyas.

Al-Zarqa presents two concrete cases where Hanafi jurists apply istihsan qiyasi. The first involves a common debt owed by one debtor to two creditors; the second contrasts debt collection with deposit return. In each, the manifest analogy would lead to a different result than the hidden, subtler analogy that is ultimately adopted.

Guided Path
1
Examine the common debt scenario
State the facts: One debtor owes a debt to two creditors jointly. One creditor receives his share. The received amount perishes before the second creditor takes his share. Manifest qiyas would split the loss between both creditors because they share the debt. Istihsan says the loss is borne only by the receiving creditor.
Identify the hidden qiyas: The second creditor was never obligated to share in the risk of the received amount; his claim remains against the debtor.
2
Identify the manifest and hidden qiyas in the debt case
Manifest qiyas: The received amount is seen as belonging to both creditors in proportion, so loss is shared. Hidden qiyas: The second creditor's right is not attached to the specific property but to the debtor's dhimma. Therefore, he cannot be forced to share the risk of that specific property.
The hidden qiyas is stronger because it respects the nature of the claim (dhimma vs. specific property).
3
Examine the deposit example
Facts: A depositor goes absent. A person claims to be his agent to collect the deposit. The depositary (bailee) admits the agency. Manifest qiyas (analogy to debt) would force the depositary to hand over the deposit. Istihsan says he is not obliged.
Contrast with debt: If the debtor admits an agent and pays, and the creditor later denies, the debtor must pay again but can recover from the false agent. In deposit, if the depositary hands over and the owner denies, the depositary loses the specific item entirely, as his right is 'ayni (specific property).
4
Identify the hidden qiyas in the deposit case
Manifest qiyas: Extend the rule from debt – admission of agency forces delivery. Hidden qiyas: In deposit, the owner's right is attached to the specific object ('ayn), not the dhimma. Handing over could cause irreparable loss. Therefore, the hidden qiyas protects the depositary.
The hidden qiyas is stronger because it considers the different nature of the right (specific property vs. liability).
5
Generalize the principle of istihsan qiyasi
In both examples, the hidden qiyas is preferred because it is more precise: it correctly identifies the nature of the legal relationship (dhimma vs. 'ayn) and achieves a more equitable outcome. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of tarjih between analogies.

Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
And the meaning of that is that istihsan is turning away from the ruling of qiyas in a case to another ruling due to a reason that necessitates this turning. Indeed, istihsan is detaching the case from its analogical counterparts. It is the opposite of manifest qiyas, which is: attaching the case to its counterparts in ruling. Based on the type of cause (illa) for which the istihsani case is detached from its analogical counterparts, istihsan is divided into two types: qiyasi (analogical) istihsan and daruri (necessity) istihsan. (1)
First Request: Istihsan Qiyasi
3/4 - As for istihsan qiyasi, it is that one turns away from the ruling of the manifest, readily apparent qiyas in the case to a different ruling by another qiyas that is subtler and more hidden than the first, but it is stronger in proof, sounder in consideration, and more correct in conclusion. Due to the prevalence of this type of istihsan in the method of Hanafi jurists, some of them restrict the definition of istihsan to being 'hidden qiyas'. This type of istihsan in reality is but a preference for one qiyas over another when there are multiple aspects of qiyas and they conflict in a single case. So it is from qiyas and to it.
4/4 - Examples of Istihsan Qiyasi:
Among the examples of istihsan qiyasi are the following cases:
1 - Indeed, the common debt (2) - if one of the creditors receives the amount of his share, he does not have the right to exclusively keep it; rather, his partner in the debt can demand from him his share of what was received. If what was received perishes in the hand of the receiver before the second partner takes his share from it, the requirement of manifest qiyas would be that it perishes from the account of both, because just as they share the received amount if it remains safe, they should jointly bear the burden of its loss if it perishes. But in istihsan, what perishes in the hand of the receiver is considered perished only from his share, and the share that was not received belongs to the second partner. This is because originally he was not obligated to share with the receiver in what he received; rather, he could leave the received amount to the receiver and pursue the debtor for his share.
2 - It is an established rule that a person is bound by his admission regarding his own rights, not regarding the rights of others. So if, for example, someone admits that he and his brother owe a sum of money, he is liable for his portion of it, but his brother is not liable if he denies. Based on this, if someone claims to be an agent for an absent creditor to collect his debt, and the debtor admits his agency, he is ordered to pay the debt to him based on his admission. And accordingly, if someone deposits something with another and then goes absent, and a person claims to be the agent of the absent one to collect his deposit, and the depositary admits his agency, the requirement of manifest qiyas, based on the case of debt collection, would be to obligate the depositary to hand over the deposit to him. But istihsan dictates not obligating the depositary to hand over the deposit to him, even if the depositary admits his agency, due to the possibility that the owner of the deposit might appear and deny the agency, and his deposit would be gone and perhaps could not be retrieved, and his right is attached to the specific object. Unlike the case of debt, where the right of the creditor is attached to the debtor's liability (dhimma), not to the specific amount that this debtor pays to the supposed agent for collection. If the creditor appears and denies the agency, it becomes clear that the earlier payment was not a valid discharge of the debt, because the agent's agency was not established, so the creditor's right remains as it was in the debtor's liability, and he is required to pay again to the creditor, and he has the right to recourse against the receiver to retrieve what he paid him. So he is ordered to pay again to the one who denied the agency. And the clarification of that is that the process of discharging a debt, in reality and from a juristic perspective, is that...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, explaining istihsan (juristic preference) as a secondary source of Islamic law. It defines istihsan as departing from the ruling of qiyas (analogy) in a case to another ruling due to a stronger reason. Istihsan is essentially detaching the case from its analogical counterparts (nazair), opposite to manifest qiyas which attaches the case to its counterparts. Based on the nature of the cause (illa) justifying the departure, istihsan is divided into two types: istihsan qiyasi (analogical istihsan) and istihsan al-darura (necessity istihsan). The passage then focuses on istihsan qiyasi, which is the most common type in the Hanafi school. It occurs when a case is taken away from the apparent manifest qiyas to a different ruling through another qiyas that is subtler and more hidden but stronger in evidence and reasoning. This type is essentially a preference (tarjih) between conflicting analogies. Some Hanafi scholars even define istihsan as 'hidden qiyas'. The passage then provides two examples. The first example concerns a common debt (dayn mushtarak) owed by one debtor to two creditors. If one creditor receives his share and it is destroyed before the other takes his share, manifest qiyas would require the loss to be shared. But istihsan considers the loss only from the receiver's share because the second creditor was never obligated to share the risk. The second example contrasts two situations: debt vs. deposit. If a person claims to be an agent of an absent creditor and the debtor admits and pays, then if the creditor appears and denies, the debtor must pay again and can seek recourse from the false agent. But in the case of a deposit, if a person claims to be an agent for the absent owner and the depositary admits and delivers the deposit, istihsan protects the depositary from liability because the right is attached to the specific item, unlike debt which is an obligation in the dhimma. So the depositary is not forced to hand over, otherwise the owner might lose his property entirely. These examples illustrate how istihsan qiyasi selects a more nuanced analogy over a superficial one.

Key Terms
الدين المشترك (al-dayn al-mushtarak): ما ثبت لاثنين فأكثر في ذمة ثالث بسبب متحد
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): القياس الأقوى حجة وإن كان أخفى من القياس الظاهر
الاستحسان القياسي (al-istihsan al-qiyasi): العدول عن حكم القياس الظاهر إلى حكم مغاير بقياس آخر أدق وأخفى وأقوى حجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the depositary's admission is invalid in deposit cases.
B) Because the owner's right is attached to the specific object, so handing over could cause irreparable loss.

Key Takeaway
The two examples demonstrate that istihsan qiyasi selects the analogy that best respects the underlying nature of the legal right (dhimma vs. 'ayn), achieving a more just outcome.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas in Loss Among Creditors
Example of istihsan overriding qiyas in loss of goods received

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that istihsan overrides qiyas in the case of lost goods received by one partner, and derive the fatwa ruling for the scenario.

Core Idea
Istihsan protects the non-receiving partner: loss is on the receiver alone.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi example of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding apparent qiyas (analogy). The scenario involves two partners in a debt, where one creditor receives payment but the goods are destroyed before the second partner collects his share. While qiyas would split the loss, istihsan places it on the receiver to avoid hardship to the non-receiving partner. Understanding this example illuminates how istihsan operates as a subsidiary source in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two partners share a debt. One creditor receives payment (goods) but the goods are destroyed before the second partner takes his share. Determine who bears the loss under different legal methods.
The key fact is that only one creditor took possession.
2
State the apparent qiyas
Apply simple analogy: since both partners jointly owned the debt, they should share both benefit and risk. So the loss should be split between them.
Qiyas here treats the received goods as joint property.
3
State the istihsan ruling
The Hanafi position (istihsan) holds that the loss is borne solely by the receiver, because the other partner was not obligated to join in taking possession.
Istihsan prioritizes the principle that one is only liable for what they choose to possess.
4
Identify the dalil for istihsan
The underlying evidence is the removal of hardship: if loss were shared, the non-receiving partner would be penalized for the receiver's sole action. Istihsan here draws on a stronger consideration (defraying harm).
This is a form of istihsan based on darurah (necessity) or maslahah (interest).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical fatwa consequence: the non-receiving partner maintains his right to pursue the debtor for his full share, undiminished by the loss.
This result protects the one who did not take possession.

Commentary
This passage provides an example of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi fiqh. The scenario involves two partners in a debt: one creditor receives payment from the debtor, but the goods are destroyed before the other creditor takes his share. According to apparent qiyas, the loss should be shared between the two creditors, since they would share the benefit had it been safe. However, istihsan rules that the loss is borne only by the receiver, because the other partner was not obligated to participate in taking possession; he could have left the goods with the receiver and pursued the debtor for his share. This ruling is based on the principle that one's choice to take possession implies bearing the risk. The authority weight of this ruling is from later Hanafi works (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin), as it is drawn from explanations of istihsan in usul texts.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas: No Liability After Debt Release
Istihsan overrides qiyas on mortgagee liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to override apparent qiyas in the case of mortgagee liability after debt release, and construct the qiyas panel for both the apparent analogy and the istihsan-based ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan: the mortgagee who releases the debt is like one who dissolves the mortgage — no liability without negligence.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi application of istihsan to override the apparent qiyas in the law of mortgage (rahn). According to clear analogy, the mortgagee would remain liable for the mortgaged property even after releasing the debtor, just as he would after collecting the debt. But the Hanafi school, using istihsan, rules that the mortgagee is not liable unless he is negligent. This is because by releasing the debt, he effectively cancels the mortgage, making the property a trust in his hands. Understanding this example trains the mufti to recognize when istihsan can override qiyas and how to articulate the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The default rule: the mortgagee is liable for the mortgaged property up to the value of the debt. This liability continues even after the debt is collected until the property is returned.
This is the baseline.
2
State the apparent qiyas
By apparent qiyas, the case of release is analogized to the case of collection: since the property remains guaranteed after collection, it should also remain guaranteed after release.
This is the opposing argument (the 'apparent qiyas').
3
Identify the istihsan ruling
Istihsan overrides qiyas: the mortgagee is NOT liable after release because he is considered to have dissolved the mortgage contract. The property becomes a trust (amanah).
This is the Hanafi position.
4
Analyse the legal rationale
The distinction: release dissolves the mortgage, while collection does not. The mortgagee has the right to cancel the mortgage unilaterally. With cancellation, the property becomes a trust, so liability only for negligence.
This is the farq (distinction).
5
Construct the qiyas panel for both views
List the asl, far', illa, and hukm for the apparent qiyas. Then note that istihsan rejects the hukm of qiyas due to a stronger consideration (dissolution of mortgage).
Use the qiyas_panel to structure this analysis.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - من المقرَّر فقهاً أنَّ المرهون مضمون على الدائن المرتهن بما يعادل الدين، فإذا هَلَكَ المرهون في يده، وكانت قيمته مساوية للذين سقط إنَّ المرتهن لو كان قد استوفى الدين قبل هلاك المرهون يرد الدين حتى ما استوفاه. وعلى هذا لو أبرأ الدائن المرتهن ذمَّة المدين عن دينه، ثم هلك المرهون قبل إعادته، فإنَّ مقتضى القياس الظاهر أن يضمن المرتهن للراهن قيمته قياساً لحالة الإبراء على حالة الاستيفاء، إذ يبقى المرهون مضموناً بعد استيفاء الدين حتى يعاد. ولكن الاستحسان عدم ضمان المرهون بعد الإبراء عن الدين، واعتبار المرتهن بعد إبرائه للمدين كالفاسخ للرهن لأن الدائن المرتهن يستقل بفسخ الرهن، إذ هو توثيق لحقه، وإذا فسخه انقلب المرهون أمانة في يده، فلا يضمن هلاكه عندئذ إلا بالتعدي عليه أو التقصير في حفظه (ر: رد المحتار ٣٣٥/٥ و .(۳۳۸
3 - It is established juristically that the mortgaged property is guaranteed by the creditor-mortgagee to the extent of the debt. So if the mortgaged property is destroyed in his hand, and its value equals the debt, then if the mortgagee had collected the debt before the destruction of the mortgaged property, he would have to return the debt, even what he collected. Based on this, if the creditor-mortgagee releases the debtor's liability from the debt, then the mortgaged property is destroyed before its return, then the requirement of apparent analogy is that the mortgagee is liable to the mortgagor for its value, analogizing the case of release to the case of collection, because the mortgaged property remains guaranteed after collection of the debt until it is returned. But istihsan is that there is no liability for the mortgaged property after release from the debt, and considering the mortgagee after his release of the debtor as one who has dissolved the mortgage, because the creditor-mortgagee has the authority to dissolve the mortgage unilaterally, since it is a security for his right. And if he dissolves it, the mortgaged property becomes a trust in his hand, so he is not liable for its destruction at that time except by transgression or negligence in its preservation. (Radd al-Muhtar 5/335 and 338).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents another example of istihsan overriding qiyas in Hanafi fiqh, this time concerning the liability of a mortgagee (creditor) after releasing the debtor from the debt. According to apparent qiyas, the mortgagee should be liable for the mortgaged property if it is destroyed after release, just as he would be if he had actually collected the debt. But istihsan rules that the mortgagee is not liable, because by releasing the debtor, he effectively dissolves the mortgage himself. Once the mortgage is dissolved, the mortgaged property becomes a trust (amanah) in his hands, and he is only liable if he commits misconduct or negligence. This ruling is based on the principle that the mortgagee has the right to cancel the mortgage unilaterally, as it is for his own security. The authority weight is from later Hanafi works (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin), specifically Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): توثيق دين بعين يمكن استيفاء الدين من ثمنها عند الحاجة.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): إسقاط الدين عن المدين من قبل الدائن.

In Hanafi muamalat, istihsan can override apparent qiyas when a stronger legal rationale (here, dissolution of the mortgage) justifies a different outcome.

Istihsan: Turning from Qiyas to Prevent Hardship
Defines istihsan and its role as a corrective to qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihsan as a secondary source, explain its rationale, and identify when it is applied to avoid hardship from strict qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan is a disciplined departure from qiyas to achieve a ruling aligned with maqasid and prevent hardship.

In this lesson, we explore istihsan (juristic preference), one of the secondary sources of Hanafi law. The passage explains that istihsan is invoked when the strict application of analogy (qiyas) would lead to hardship or problematic outcomes. By turning to a different ruling via istihsan, the jurist ensures that the law remains just and practical. We will see that this method is rooted in the broader theory of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest).

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
When does istihsan become necessary? Look for 'حرج' or 'مشكلة' (hardship/problem) resulting from qiyas.
The passage uses the phrase 'اطراد الحكم القياسي مؤدياً لحرج'.
2
Define the solution
What does istihsan do? It 'يعدل' (turns away) from the qiyasi ruling to another ruling that removes the hardship.
Istihsan literally means 'seeking the better'.
3
Understand the rationale
Why can outcomes differ? Because issues, though analogized, have different contexts and circumstances ('باختلاف موضوعاتها وما يكتنفها من عوارض وملابسات').
4
Connect to maqasid
How does istihsan serve the objectives of Sharia? It aligns with 'المنطق الفقهي ومقاصد الشريعة'.
It is not arbitrary but principled.
5
Link to maslaha mursala
The author states this type of istihsan returns to the theory of maslaha mursala, to be explained later.
This shows istihsan is grounded in public interest.

Source Text

الفصل (٤) المصادر التبعية الاستحسان
فمحله عندما يكون اطراد الحكم القياسي مؤدياً لحرج أو مشكلة في بعض المسائل؛ فيعدل حينئذ عنه استحساناً إلى حكم آخر يزول به الحرج وتندفع به المشكلة وذلك لأن المسائل التي يقاس بعضها على بعض - وإن كانت من جنس واحد وقائمة على أسس مشتركة - قد تختلف نتائجها عدلاً وجَوْراً، أو عسراً ويسراً باختلاف موضوعاتها وما يكتنفها من عوارض
وملابسات .
فالاستحسان يكون في مثل هذا طريقاً للفقهاء إلى الأحكام المصلحية التي تتفق مع المنطق الفقهي ومقاصد الشريعة عندما يلوح في اطراد القياس سوء النتائج.
وهذا النوع من الاستحسان يرجع في الحقيقة إلى نظرية المصالح
المرسلة الآتي بيانها في البحث التالي، كما سنرى.
Chapter (4) Secondary Sources: Istihsan. Its place is when the continuous application of a qiyasi ruling leads to hardship or a problem in some issues; then one turns away from it by istihsan to another ruling that removes the hardship and solves the problem. This is because issues that are analogized to each other—even if of the same type and based on common foundations—may differ in their outcomes in terms of justice/injustice or hardship/ease depending on their subjects and surrounding circumstances. So istihsan becomes in such a case a path for jurists to beneficial rulings that agree with fiqh logic and the objectives of the Sharia when the continuous application of qiyas shows bad outcomes. This type of istihsan actually returns to the theory of maslaha mursala which will be explained in the next research, as we shall see.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage defines istihsan (juristic preference) as one of the secondary sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi school. The author explains that istihsan is applied when strictly following qiyas (analogy) would lead to hardship or problematic results. In such situations, the jurist turns away from the analogical ruling and adopts another ruling that removes the hardship and solves the problem. The reason is that even though issues may be analogized to each other, their outcomes can differ based on context and circumstances. Thus, istihsan allows the jurist to achieve rulings that serve the objectives of the Sharia (maqasid) when qiyas would lead to harmful results. The author notes that this type of istihsan essentially falls under the theory of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest), which will be discussed later.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A secondary source of Islamic law: turning away from the ruling of an analogy to another ruling that the mujtahid deems better or more suitable for removing hardship or achieving public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for applying istihsan?
A) To follow a weaker opinion for ease
B) To avoid hardship or problematic outcomes resulting from qiyas
C) To always prefer the opinion of the majority
D) To replace qiyas entirely

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is a legitimate Hanafi method to depart from qiyas when it leads to hardship, ensuring the law serves the purposes of Sharia.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

Istihsan: Definition, Examples, and Critique of Traditional Division
Critique of traditional istihsan classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two authentic types of istihsan (qiyasi and darurah) and the misnamed categories 'istihsan al-sunna' and 'istihsan al-ijma', and explain why Mustafa al-Zarqa refines the definition.

Core Idea
True istihsan is a corrective to qiyas, not a catch-all for any departure from qiyas.

In this passage, Mustafa al-Zarqa explains the concept of istihsan (juristic preference) as a subsidiary source in Hanafi law. He provides concrete examples where istihsan overrides strict qiyas to avoid hardship. Then he critiques the traditional classification of istihsan into four types, arguing that only two are genuine: qiyasi (preferring hidden analogy) and darurah (necessity). This refinement clarifies the term's technical meaning and prevents confusion with primary sources like sunna and ijma.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two authentic types of istihsan
From the examples provided (agency offsetting and bread borrowing), identify that istihsan operates in two ways: preferring a hidden analogy (qiyasi) or considering necessity (darurah). Note that the bread example is based on necessity, not a hidden analogy, illustrating the darurah type.
The author uses these examples to demonstrate the real function of istihsan as a corrective to strict qiyas.
2
Analyze the rationale behind istihsan
Understand that istihsan overrides qiyas to prevent hardship or to follow a stronger evidence. In the agency example, offsetting is allowed by istihsan to facilitate aid. In the bread example, necessity overrides the prohibition of riba because the weight variation is trivial in custom.
Istihsan is always a departure from the apparent qiyas to a more suitable ruling.
3
Review the traditional four-part classification
Learn that many Hanafi usul scholars divide istihsan into four types: qiyasi, darurah, sunna, and ijma. Under this view, any departure from qiyas to a ruling based on sunna or ijma is also considered istihsan.
This classification is found in works like Kashf al-Asrar by al-Bazdawi.
4
Engage with Zarqa's critique
Read Zarqa's argument: the ruling in cases of sunna or ijma is directly from those sources, not from the methodology of istihsan. Istihsan is specifically a tool to correct qiyas when qiyas would lead to harsh or unreasonable results. Labeling sunna- or ijma-based rulings as istihsan is an 'insertion in the wrong place' (إقحام في غير محله).
This critique hinges on the epistemological difference between a primary source (sunna/ijma) and a corrective method (istihsan).
5
Apply the refined definition
Given a new scenario, determine whether a ruling should be labeled as istihsan or attributed directly to another source. For example, a ruling based on a prophetic hadith is not istihsan but a direct application of sunna. This sharpens your use of legal terminology and prevents conceptual confusion.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that a mufti must correctly identify the basis of a ruling to ensure consistent methodology.

Chapter (4): Subsidiary Sources – Istihsan
He ordered the payer with the intention to recover later from what he paid; the apparent qiyas is that the ordered person is considered a donor and returns what he took from the orderer. But they said that in istihsan he is not considered a donor, to facilitate aid and remove hardship in its path, so offsetting occurs between what he paid from his wealth and what he has in his hand of the orderer's wealth (Radd al-Muhtar, book of agency, 4/415).
3. Goods measured by volume or weight are legally considered ribawi goods in which riba al-fadl applies, i.e., it is not permissible to lend any of them and recover more. Likewise, it is not permissible to sell some of them for a greater amount of the same type. But Hanafi jurists ruled that borrowing bread by number among neighbors is permissible, even if the weights of loaves vary in the usual way, by istihsan contrary to qiyas, due to necessity and people's need combined with the absence of the idea of riba and profit-seeking in this transaction, because this variation is among the trivialities customarily overlooked (1). (Radd al-Muhtar 4/172 and 187). The Maliki ijtihad also went to this.

(1) Such should be considered in exchanging silver coins and the like with their smaller parts when the total weight of the parts is less or more than the weight of the replaced piece. Today some incorrectly hesitate in this, exaggerating and being unnecessarily strict in religion, even though this exchange is more needed and more deserving of legal permissibility than borrowing bread by number among neighbors, because the replaced parts and the coin piece are equal in value and custom, and this does not serve as a means for usury and profit-seeking.
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh
Concerning this, the jurists say: When it is mentioned in an issue that the ruling in it is such by qiyas, and its opposite by istihsan, then the ruling of istihsan is the preponderant and always acted upon. That is because istihsan in reality is a remedy for the problems that may arise from qiyas in rulings sometimes.
4/8 – Critique of the Traditional Division of Istihsan:
Now, after we have known from the above explanation the true meaning of istihsan and its rank among the sources and evidences of rulings, in that it is in reality a corrective method to address the extremism and harms resulting from the regularity of qiyas in some issues, we say: Most Hanafi usul scholars divide istihsan into four categories, adding to the two explained types two other types:
- Istihsan al-sunna: in their view, it is turning away from the ruling of qiyas to a contrary ruling established in the sunna.
- Istihsan al-ijma: also turning away from the requirement of qiyas to another ruling on which there is consensus, as in the validity of the istisna' contract previously mentioned in the discussion of ijma (1).
It is not hidden that generalization and diversification in the meaning of technical istihsan is unsound, and it is an insertion of something in the wrong place.
It is clear from what was explained that the ruling established in what they call istihsan al-sunna or istihsan al-ijma is attributed to sunna or ijma, i.e., to the text of the Lawgiver and what is similar to it, not to qiyas or istihsan.
(1) See: Kashf al-Asrar by Allama Sheikh Abd al-Aziz al-Bukhari, commentary on Usul al-Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, 3/4, and the book Abu Hanifa by Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra, part two, p. 174.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of istihsan (juristic preference) as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. It begins by providing examples of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh: the case where a person ordered to pay money is not considered a donor but rather offsetting occurs, and the case of borrowing bread by number among neighbors despite the usual weight variation, which is permitted by istihsan due to necessity despite the general prohibition of riba. The author then notes that these examples illustrate two types of istihsan: qiyasi istihsan (where a hidden analogy is preferred over a superficial one) and necessity istihsan (based on need). He asserts that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas when they conflict. On page 92, the author critiques the traditional division of istihsan into four categories as held by most Hanafi usul scholars. He argues that adding 'istihsan al-sunna' and 'istihsan al-ijma' is unsound because rulings based on sunna or ijma are attributed to those sources themselves, not to istihsan as a separate methodological tool. True istihsan is only a corrective to qiyas, not a label for any departure from qiyas. This is a critical refinement: the author restricts the definition of istihsan to its core function of modifying strict qiyas in light of other considerations.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): العدول عن حكم القياس إلى حكم آخر أقوى دليلاً أو لدفع حرج، وهو عند المؤلف نوعان: استحسان قياسي (ترجيح القياس الخفي على الجلي) واستحسان ضرورة (مراعاة الحاجة والعرف).
القياس (al-qiyas): إلحاق فرع بأصل في حكم لعلة جامعة، وهو الدليل العقلي في الفقه. الاستحسان يعدل عن قياس ظاهر إلى حكم آخر.
استحسان السنة (istihsan al-sunna): عند بعض الحنفية: العدول عن حكم القياس إلى حكم ثبت في السنة. والمؤلف يرى أنه ليس استحساناً اصطلاحياً بل حكم مستند إلى السنة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Mustafa al-Zarqa reject considering 'istihsan al-sunna' and 'istihsan al-ijma' as valid types of istihsan?
A) Because sunna and ijma may occasionally contradict each other.
B) Because the ruling in those cases is directly attributed to sunna or ijma, not to the methodology of istihsan.
C) Because the Hanafi school does not accept sunna or ijma as sources.
D) Because istihsan only applies to matters of worship, not transactions.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan in its technical sense is only a corrective to qiyas, either by preferring a hidden analogy (qiyasi) or by considering necessity (darurah); rulings based on sunna or ijma are not istihsan.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
