Critique of the Traditional Division of Istihsan
Critiquing the four-fold classification of istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of istihsan according to some Hanafis, critique the inclusion of sunna- and ijma-based istihsan, and apply the correct Hanafi usul principle that true istihsan is only the jurist's departure from qiyas in the absence of primary texts.

Core Idea
Genuine istihsan is the jurist's corrective to qiyas; rulings from sunna or ijma must not be rebranded as istihsan.

In this lesson, we examine a common classification of istihsan into four types and the critique that only two are valid. Understanding this distinction is crucial for muftis to correctly attribute rulings to their proper sources and avoid conflating primary and secondary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the traditional four-fold division
Identify the four types of istihsan as presented by some Hanafi usul scholars: based on hidden qiyas, necessity, sunna, and ijma.
2
Understand the author's objection
The author argues that sunna and ijma are primary sources that take precedence over qiyas, so rulings from them should be attributed directly to those sources, not to istihsan.
3
Distinguish between istihsan al-shari' and istihsan al-faqih
Istihsan al-shari' is the Lawgiver's own preference embedded in texts; istihsan al-faqih is the jurist's inference in the absence of a text. Only the latter is truly istihsan.
4
Apply the critique to fatwa practice
When issuing fatwas, ensure that rulings based on explicit texts or consensus are not labeled as istihsan, to maintain clarity in the hierarchy of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن هذا يقول الفقهاء: إذا ذكر في مسألة أنّ الحكم فيها كذا قياساً، وعكسه استحساناً، فحكم الاستحسان هو الراجح المعمول به دائماً. وذلك لأن الاستحسان في الحقيقة إنما هو علاج لما قد يترتب على القياس من مشكلات الأحكام في بعض الأحيان.
٨/٤ - نقد التقسيم التقليدي للاستحسان :
هذا، وبعد أن عرفنا مما سبق بيانه حقيقة معنى الاستحسان ورتبته في مصادر الأحكام وأدلتها من حيث إنه في الحقيقة طريقة تعديلية لمعالجة ما يؤدي إليه اطراد القياس في بعض المسائل من غلو ومساوىء، نقول: إن معظم علماء أصول الفقه الحنفي يقسمون الاستحسان إلى أربعة أقسام، فيزيدون على هذين النوعين المشروحَيْن نوعين آخرين هما:
- استحسان السنة، وهو لديهم عدول عن حكم القياس إلى حكم مخالف له ثبت في السنة .
- واستحسان الإجماع، وهو عدول أيضاً عن مقتضي القياس إلى حكم آخر انعقد عليه الإجماع، كما في صحة عقد الاستصناع المتقدم ذكره في بحث الإجماع.
ولا يخفى أن التعميم والتنويع في معنى الاستحسان الاصطلاحي غير سديد، وهو إقحام للشيء في غير محله. فمن الواضح بعدما سبق بيانه أن الحكم الثابت فيما يسمونه استحسان السنة أو استحسان الإجماع، إنما يضاف ثبوته إلى السنة أو الإجماع، أي إلى نص الشارع وما في حكمه، لا إلى قياس أو استحسان .
فالاستحسان المقصود إنما هو عدول من الفقيه المُسْتَنبِط عن حكم القياس حيث يجوز القياس لفقدان النص التشريعي. وإن القرآن ثم السنة ثم الإجماع مصادر ثلاثة أساسية مقدمة في الرتبة على القياس، فلا مجال لقياس ولا استحسان إلا فيما لم يرد من الأحكام في أحد تلك المصادر الثلاثة. فإطلاق اسم الاستحسان على هذين النوعين هو حشر للشيء في غير زمرته، وتوسع في لفظ الاستحسان يورث اشتباهاً في تمييز الحقائق. على أنَّ ما ورد به النص منحرفاً عن قياس أمثاله لمصلحة لحظها الشارع إنما هو في الحقيقة استحسان الشارع وليس الكلام فيه، وإنما الكلام في استحسان الفقيه المستنبط الذي يطبق نصوص الشارع ويقيس عليها، ويستحسن على وفقها، مستلهماً من غرض الشارع ومقاصد شريعته.
٩/٤ - وقد اشتهر أبو حنيفة وأتباعه من فقهاء مدرسته بطريقة الاستحسان وبناء الأحكام عليها وبَرَعوا في الاستنباط الاستحساني براعة عدلوا فيها كثيراً من غلو القياس الظاهر عندما يؤدي إلى مشكلة في
And concerning this, the jurists say: when in a matter it is mentioned that the ruling is such by qiyas, and its opposite by istihsan, then the ruling of istihsan is the preponderant and perpetually acted-upon. That is because istihsan in reality is only a treatment of what may result from qiyas in terms of problematic rulings sometimes. 8/4 - Critique of the traditional division of istihsan: After we have known from the foregoing explanation the true meaning of istihsan and its rank among the sources of rulings and their evidences, in that it is in reality a corrective method to treat the excess and bad consequences that the rigid application of qiyas leads to in some issues, we say: most Hanafi usul scholars divide istihsan into four categories, adding to the two described types two more types: - Istihsan based on sunna, which according to them is departing from the ruling of qiyas to a contrary ruling established in the sunna. - And istihsan based on ijma, which is also a departure from the requirement of qiyas to another ruling on which consensus has been reached, as in the validity of the istisna'a contract mentioned previously in the discussion of ijma. It is not hidden that generalization and diversification in the meaning of technical istihsan is not sound, and it is inserting something into an improper place. It is clear after what has been explained that the ruling established in what they call istihsan of sunna or istihsan of ijma is attributed to the sunna or ijma, i.e., to the text of the Lawgiver and what is in its ruling, not to qiyas or istihsan. The intended istihsan is only the departure of the inferring jurist from the ruling of qiyas where qiyas is permissible due to the absence of a legislative text. The Qur'an, then the sunna, then ijma are three primary sources that take precedence over qiyas, so there is no room for qiyas or istihsan except in matters for which no ruling is found in any of these three sources. Thus, applying the name istihsan to these two types is placing something in the wrong group, and an expansion of the word istihsan that causes confusion in distinguishing realities. Moreover, what is stated in a text that deviates from the qiyas of its like for a benefit observed by the Lawgiver is in reality the Lawgiver's istihsan, and discussion is not about it; rather discussion is about the istihsan of the inferring jurist who applies the texts of the Lawgiver, measures by them, and exercises istihsan in accordance with them, inspired by the purpose of the Lawgiver and the objectives of His Shari'ah. 9/4 - Abu Hanifa and his followers from his school have become famous for the method of istihsan and building rulings upon it, and they excelled in istihsan-based inference, an excellence through which they corrected much of the apparent excess of qiyas when it leads to a problem.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage critiques the traditional Hanafi classification of istihsan into four types (qiyas khafi, necessity, sunna, ijma). The author, citing most Hanafi usul scholars, argues that only two types are genuine: istihsan based on hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) and istihsan based on necessity. The other two (istihsan based on sunna and ijma) are misnomers because they rely on primary textual sources—the Qur'an, sunna, and ijma—which take precedence over qiyas. True istihsan, as practiced by Abu Hanifa and his school, is the jurist's departure from an apparent qiyas ruling when it leads to a problematic outcome, using a hidden analogy or a consideration of public interest (maslaha). The author further distinguishes between the 'istihsan of the Lawgiver' (Shari'), which is embedded in revealed texts, and the 'istihsan of the inferring jurist,' which is the jurist's ijtihad. The former is not a matter of debate; it is divine legislation. The latter is the proper domain of istihsan as a subsidiary source. Abu Hanifa and his followers are renowned for their extensive use of istihsan to mitigate the harshness of strict qiyas.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): The jurist's departure from the ruling of apparent qiyas to an alternative ruling due to a hidden analogy or necessity.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared underlying cause (illa).
استحسان السنة (istihsan al-sunnah): A category used by some Hanafis for a ruling that departs from qiyas based on a specific sunna text.
استحسان الإجماع (istihsan al-ijma): A category for a ruling that departs from qiyas because there is consensus (ijma) on a contrary ruling, e.g., the validity of istisna'.
استحسان الشارع (istihsan al-shari'): The Lawgiver's own preference, embodied in revealed rulings that diverge from the general pattern of qiyas.
استحسان الفقيه المستنبِط (istihsan al-faqih al-mustanbit): The inferring jurist's exercise of istihsan, i.e., preferring a ruling over the apparent qiyas based on hidden analogy or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's critique, why is the category 'istihsan al-sunnah' problematic?
A) Because the sunna is a primary source and takes precedence over qiyas, so the ruling should be attributed directly to the sunna, not to istihsan.
B) Because the sunna never contradicts qiyas.
C) Because Abu Hanifa rejected all forms of istihsan.
D) Because istihsan al-sunnah is synonymous with ijma.

Key Takeaway
True istihsan is the jurist's departure from apparent qiyas in the absence of primary texts; rulings from sunna or ijma must be attributed directly to those sources.

Istihsan as a Subsidiary Source in Hanafi and Maliki Fiqh
Defining istihsan and comparing Hanafi and Maliki approaches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Maliki definitions of istihsan and apply the correct definition in identifying cases where istihsan is used.

Core Idea
Istihsan: departing from apparent analogy for a stronger evidence – definition and scope differ between Hanafis and Malikis.

Istihsan is a subsidiary source of Islamic law that allows a jurist to depart from the ruling of apparent analogy (qiyas) when strict application leads to hardship or injustice. This lesson unpacks the definition from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam, comparing how the Hanafi and Maliki schools conceptualize istihsan, and clarifying that it is not arbitrary opinion but a reasoned departure grounded in stronger evidence or public interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and scope of istihsan
Read the first paragraph: istihsan is the jurist's departure from qiyas when no text exists. Note that it is subsidiary to Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.
Istihsan only applies where there is no ruling from primary sources.
2
Distinguish the two types of istihsan
The author distinguishes istihsan of the Lawgiver (Shari') from istihsan of the jurist. Focus on the latter, which is the subject of ijtihad.
3
Compare Hanafi and Maliki definitions
Hanafis include hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) under istihsan; Malikis restrict it to leaving apparent qiyas for custom, maslaha, or hardship. Note the common core: preferring a stronger evidence or maslaha.
The difference is terminological; both schools recognize the same underlying principle.
4
Ground istihsan in Sharia objectives
The passage cites Quranic verses and the hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' to show that istihsan serves the goals of ease, removal of hardship, and public interest.
5
Apply the definition to a hypothetical case
Given a scenario with no explicit text, determine whether istihsan would apply and which school's definition would be used in fatwa.
Practice applying the conceptual framework.

الفصل (٤) المصادر التبعية الاستحسان
فالاستحسان المقصود إنما هو عدول من الفقيه المُسْتَنبِط عن حكم القياس حيث يجوز القياس لفقدان النص التشريعي. وإن القرآن ثم السنة ثم الإجماع مصادر ثلاثة أساسية مقدمة في الرتبة على القياس، فلا مجال لقياس ولا استحسان إلا فيما لم يرد من الأحكام في أحد تلك المصادر الثلاثة. فإطلاق اسم الاستحسان على هذين النوعين هو حشر للشيء في غير زمرته، وتوسع في لفظ الاستحسان يورث اشتباهاً في تمييز الحقائق (۱) . على أنَّ ما ورد به النص منحرفاً عن قياس أمثاله لمصلحة لحظها الشارع الأمر إنما هو في الحقيقة استحسان الشارع وليس الكلام فيه، وإنما الكلام في استحسان الفقيه المستنبط الذي يطبق نصوص الشارع ويقيس عليها، ويستحسن على وفقها، مستلهماً من غرض الشارع ومقاصد شريعته (۲) .
٩/٤ - وقد اشتهر أبو حنيفة وأتباعه من فقهاء مدرسته بطريقة الاستحسان وبناء الأحكام عليها وبَرَعوا في الاستنباط الاستحساني براعة عدلوا فيها كثيراً من غلو القياس الظاهر عندما يؤدي إلى مشكلة في المصلحة التطبيقية (۱). وقد أخذ الاجتهاد المالكي أيضاً بطريقة الاستحسان وتوسع فيها أكثر من الحنفية علاجاً لغلو القياس. ولكن المالكية لا يسمون القياس الخفي استحساناً كما في اصطلاح الحنفية، وإنما الاستحسان عند المالكية أن يترك القياس الظاهر لأحد أمور ثلاثة : إذا عارضه عُرْف غالب، أي عادة شائعة. أو عارضته مصلحة راجحة. أو أدى إلى حرج ومشقة. فيكون الحكم الاستحساني عندهم أيضاً من قبيل ترجيح مصلحة جزئية في حكم معين كانت تقضي القواعد القياسية بخلافه. وذلك لأن نصوص الشريعة الإسلامية تضافرت على وجوب رعاية المصلحة ودفع الحرج. كقوله تعالى : يريد الله بكم اليسر ولا يريد بكم العسر (سورة البقرة (١٨٥/٢) وقوله أيضاً : وما جعل عليكم في الدين من حرج (سورة الحج (۷۸/۲۲) وقول النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: (لا ضرر ولا ضرار) (۲) قال القاضي ابن رشد الحفيد المالكي في بداية المجتهد (١٥٤/٢) : ومعنى الاستحسان في أكثر الأحوال هو الالتفات إلى المصلحة والعدل.
Chapter (4): The Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan. So the intended istihsan is the departure of the deducing jurist from the ruling of analogy where analogy is permissible due to the absence of legislative text. The Quran, then the Sunnah, then Ijma are three primary sources that precede qiyas in rank, so there is no field for qiyas or istihsan except in matters for which no ruling has come in any of those three sources. Calling both types istihsan is placing a thing in a group not its own, and expansion of the term istihsan causes confusion in distinguishing realities (1). However, what is stated by the text, deviating from analogy of its likes for a maslaha intended by the Lawgiver, is in fact istihsan of the Lawgiver, and the discussion is not about that; rather the discussion is about the istihsan of the deducing jurist who applies the texts of the Lawgiver and makes analogies based on them, and exercises istihsan in accordance with them, inspired by the purpose of the Lawgiver and the objectives of His Sharia (2). 9/4 - Abu Hanifa and his followers from the jurists of his school became famous for the method of istihsan and building rulings upon it, and they excelled in istihsani deduction with a proficiency by which they corrected much of the excess of apparent qiyas when it leads to a problem in practical maslaha (1). The Maliki ijtihad also adopted the method of istihsan and expanded it more than the Hanafis to remedy the excess of qiyas. But the Malikis do not call hidden analogy istihsan as in the Hanafi terminology; rather, istihsan according to the Malikis is to leave the apparent qiyas for one of three matters: if it is opposed by a prevailing custom, i.e., a widespread practice; or if it is opposed by a preponderant maslaha; or if it leads to hardship and difficulty. So the istihsani ruling according to them also falls under the category of preferring a particular maslaha in a specific ruling that the qiyas rules would have dictated otherwise. This is because the texts of Islamic Sharia have concurred on the obligation of observing maslaha and removing hardship. Like His statement: 'Allah intends for you ease and does not intend for you hardship' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185) and also His statement: 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' (Surah al-Hajj 22:78) and the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No harm and no reciprocating harm' (2). Judge Ibn Rushd the grandson (Maliki) said in Bidayat al-Mujtahid (2/154): 'The meaning of istihsan in most cases is turning to maslaha and justice.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Aam addresses the concept of istihsan as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. The author begins by defining istihsan as the jurist's departure from the ruling of qiyas (analogy) when qiyas would be applicable in the absence of a direct text from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. Istihsan is not a primary source; it only comes into play when there is no ruling from those three. The author warns against loosely applying the term 'istihsan' to any deviation from qiyas; he distinguishes between two types: istihsan of the Lawgiver (Shari') where the Lawgiver Himself has provided a ruling that deviates from the apparent analogy for a maslaha – this is not the subject of debate. The subject is istihsan of the jurist, who, when applying the texts and analogizing, may occasionally depart from the apparent qiyas in light of the higher objectives of the Sharia.

The author then notes that Abu Hanifa and his followers became famous for using istihsan extensively to mitigate harsh results of strict qiyas. The Maliki school also adopted istihsan and used it even more broadly. However, the Hanafi and Maliki definitions differ: Hanafis consider hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) as a form of istihsan, while Malikis define istihsan as abandoning apparent qiyas for one of three reasons: a prevailing custom (urf), a preponderant maslaha, or to avoid hardship. The common element is that istihsan seeks to achieve maslaha and remove hardship, supported by Quranic verses and the hadith 'La darar wa la dirar'.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Departure of the jurist from the ruling of apparent qiyas to a different ruling due to a stronger evidence or maslaha.
القياس الظاهر (al-qiyas al-zahir): Apparent analogy based on clear attributes; its application may lead to harsh outcomes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition for applying istihsan in both Hanafi and Maliki fiqh?
A) The absence of any text from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma
B) The presence of a prevailing custom
C) The existence of a preponderant maslaha
D) The avoidance of hardship only

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is a disciplined departure from apparent analogy based on stronger evidence, defined and applied differently by Hanafis and Malikis, but both grounded in Sharia objectives of maslaha and hardship removal.

Definition of Istislah and Masalih Mursalah
Defining Istislah and explaining the concept of unrestricted benefits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Istislah and Masalih Mursalah, distinguish them from textually-considered benefits, and explain their role as subsidiary sources in Islamic law.

Core Idea
Istislah is building rulings on unrestricted benefits not explicitly covered by texts.

This lesson introduces two key subsidiary sources of Islamic jurisprudence: Istislah and Masalih Mursalah. Understanding these concepts is crucial for a mufti when no explicit text (nass) addresses a novel situation. We will explore their definitions, the distinction between benefits that are textually considered and those that are 'unrestricted', and the underlying idea of maslahah and mafsadah.

Guided Path
1
Define Istislah and Masalih Mursalah
Read the opening definitions: Istislah is the process of building rulings upon Masalih Mursalah. Masalih Mursalah are benefits for which no specific or generic textual evidence exists.
Note that Ghazali coined 'Istislah' to name this process.
2
Distinguish textually-considered benefits from unrestricted benefits
Identify examples of benefits established by explicit or generic text (e.g., teaching Quran, literacy) and contrast them with those that are 'mursalah' (unrestricted). The latter have no direct textual basis.
This distinction determines whether a ruling comes from text or from Istislah.
3
Analyze the concept of maslahah and mafsadah
Examine the two perspectives: intrinsic meaning (what is beneficial or harmful in itself) and Sharia's consideration (categorization into necessities, needs, and improvements).
This dual view helps evaluate whether a benefit aligns with Sharia objectives.
4
Understand the relationship between Istislah and Istihsan
Note the footnote: Istislah is a term parallel to Istihsan. Hanafis often use Istihsan for similar purposes, while Malikis apply Istislah more extensively.
This comparison highlights methodological differences between schools.

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
١/٥ - الاستصلاح هو بناء الأحكام الفقهية على مقتضى المصالح
المرسلة (١)
—
والمصالح المرسلة هي كل مصلحة لم يرد في الشرع نص على
اعتبارها بعينها أو بنوعها.
فهي إنما تدخل في عموم المصالح التي تتجلى في اجتلاب المنافع، واجتناب المضار، تلك المصالح التي جاءت الشريعة الإسلامية لتحقيقها بوجه عام ودلت نصوصها وأصولها على لزوم مراعاتها والنظر إليها في تنظيم سائر نواحي الحياة، ولم يحدد الشارع لها أفراداً ولذا سميت: مرسلة، أي مطلقة غير محددة.

Chapter Five: Subsidiary Sources: Istislah and Masalih Mursalah. Chapter Outline: Definition of Istislah; Clarifying the Idea of Benefits and Harms: a) Intrinsic meaning of benefit and harm, b) Sharia's consideration of benefit and harm: necessities, needs, and improvements; Factors prompting Istislah (blocking means and change of time); Agreement and difference between Istislah and Istihsan; Types of rulings built on the theory of Masalih Mursalah: in public administration, in the judicial system, in private rights; Istihsan and Istislah in the schools of ijtihad; Conflict of Masalih Mursalah with Sharia texts: Benefit versus definitive text, Benefit versus non-definitive text: in the Maliki school, in the Hanafi school; Appendix to this chapter: Istislah and Siyasah Shar'iyyah. Section Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. 1/5 - Istislah is building fiqh rulings upon the requirements of Masalih Mursalah (1). And Masalih Mursalah are every benefit for which no text has come in the Sharia considering it specifically or generically. Thus they only enter into the general benefits that manifest in attracting benefits and repelling harms, those benefits that the Islamic Sharia came to realize in general and whose texts and principles indicate the necessity of observing them and considering them in organizing all aspects of life, and the Lawgiver did not specify particular instances for them, hence they are called 'mursalah', i.e., absolute and unrestricted. (Y). So if a benefit has been brought by a specific text concerning it, such as writing the Quran to preserve it from loss and teaching reading and writing (2); or it was something for which a general text has come in its type that testifies to its consideration, such as the obligation of teaching knowledge and spreading it in general, and the command for all types of good and the prohibition of all kinds of evil, then in that case it is among the explicitly considered benefits (specific or generic) and not from the Masalih Mursalah, and its ruling is considered established by that text, not by the principle of Istislah. 2/5 - Clarifying the idea of Benefits and Harms. And to explain the idea of Masalih Mursalah in Islam in brief, we say: Benefit is the opposite of harm. Each of them is subject to consideration from two perspectives: (1) Imam al-Ghazali in al-Mustasfa expressed the use of the principle of Masalih Mursalah in building Sharia rulings with the term 'Istislah', and it is a new term in contrast to the word 'Istihsan', and it is better than others' expression of that with the phrase 'Masalih Mursalah' which only conveys the meaning of the benefits themselves, not the meaning of the process of building rulings upon them. (2) It is established that the Prophet had scribes of revelation who would write the Quran for him upon its revelation. It is also established that he made the ransom of the polytheist captives of Badr who knew reading and writing that each of them would teach ten of the illiterate Muslims reading and writing.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of Istislah (consideration of public benefit) and Masalih Mursalah (unrestricted benefits) as subsidiary sources of Islamic jurisprudence. The author defines Istislah as the process of deriving legal rulings based on Masalih Mursalah, which are benefits not explicitly recognized by any specific or generic textual evidence. They are distinguished from benefits that are specifically or generically mentioned in the Quran, Sunnah, or other sources. The passage then clarifies the notion of benefit (maslahah) and harm (mafsadah) from two angles: their intrinsic meaning and their legal consideration under Sharia (categorized into necessities, needs, and improvements). A footnote highlights that Imam al-Ghazali coined the term 'Istislah' to denote this process, contrasting it with 'Istihsan'. The passage concludes with examples of benefits that are textually established (e.g., teaching literacy, preserving the Quran) and thus fall outside the realm of Masalih Mursalah. The Hanafi perspective, though not detailed here, holds that Masalih Mursalah are valid as a source only when they do not contradict explicit texts and are aligned with the spirit of Sharia.

Key Terms
استصلاح (istislah): The process of building legal rulings upon the requirements of Masalih Mursalah (unrestricted benefits).
مصالح مرسلة (masalih mursalah): Benefits for which no specific or generic textual evidence exists in Sharia, but which are consistent with the general objectives of the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Benefits explicitly mentioned in the Quran
B) Benefits for which there is no specific or general textual evidence
C) Benefits that are necessary for public welfare
D) Benefits that are prohibited by sharia

Key Takeaway
Masalih Mursalah are a legitimate source when no specific or generic text exists, provided they align with Sharia objectives and do not contradict definitive texts.

Defining Al-Istislah and Al-Masalih Al-Mursalah
Defining a subsidiary source of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-istislah, distinguish between unrestricted interests (masalih mursalah) and textually indicated interests, and state the condition of absence of textual evidence for applying istislah.

Core Idea
Al-Istislah builds rulings on interests with no text, only when no specific or general text exists.

This lesson unpacks the definition of al-istislah as a subsidiary source of Islamic jurisprudence. You will learn what constitutes an 'unrestricted interest' (maslaha mursalah) and how it differs from interests supported by textual evidence. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, provides the foundational criteria that a mufti must check before invoking istislah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Read the first paragraph. Note that al-istislah is defined as building legal rulings upon 'unrestricted interests' (al-masalih al-mursalah). Understand that this is a method of legal reasoning, not a text-based source.
The Arabic term 'al-istislah' literally means 'seeking benefit'.
2
Distinguish unrestricted from textually indicated interests
The text gives two categories: interests for which no specific or general text exists (unrestricted), and those that have either a specific text (e.g., writing the Quran) or a general text (e.g., commanding all good). The ruling of the latter is based on the text, not istislah.
This distinction is crucial for correct application of istislah.
3
Apply the condition: absence of text
Istislah can only be used when there is no textual evidence considering that interest—neither specific nor general. Verify this condition in any potential case.
If a text exists, istislah is not needed; the text governs.
4
Relate to the Hanafi method
Recognize that Hanafis accept istislah but often prefer istihsan (juristic preference) when both are possible. The Hanafi approach ties maslaha closely to maqasid al-shari'ah.
The Maliki school uses istislah more extensively.

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
١/٥ - الاستصلاح هو بناء الأحكام الفقهية على مقتضى المصالح المرسلة (١)
—
والمصالح المرسلة هي كل مصلحة لم يرد في الشرع نص على اعتبارها بعينها أو بنوعها.
فهي إنما تدخل في عموم المصالح التي تتجلى في اجتلاب المنافع، واجتناب المضار، تلك المصالح التي جاءت الشريعة الإسلامية لتحقيقها بوجه عام ودلت نصوصها وأصولها على لزوم مراعاتها والنظر إليها في تنظيم سائر نواحي الحياة، ولم يحدد الشارع لها أفراداً ولذا سميت: مرسلة، أي مطلقة غير محددة.
فإذا كانت المصلحة قد جاء بها نص خاص بعينها، ككتابة القرآن صيانة له من الضياع وكتعليم القراءة والكتابة (٢)؛ أو كانت مما جاء نص عام في نوعها يشهد له بالاعتبار كوجوب تعليم العلم ونشره بوجه عام، وكالأمر بكل أنواع المعروف والنهي عن جميع فنون المنكر، فعندئذ تكون من المصالح المنصوص عليها عيناً أو نوعاً لا من المصالح المرسلة، ويعتبر حكمها ثابتاً بذلك النص لا بقاعدة الاستصلاح.
٢/٥ - إيضاح فكرة المصالح والمفاسد.
وإيضاحاً لفكرة المصالح المرسلة في الإسلام إجمالاً نقول: إنَّ المصلحة عكس المفسدة. وكل منهما محل نظر من جهتين:
- من جهة المعنى الذاتي للمصلحة والمفسدة.
- ومن جهة اعتبارهما في نظر الشارع.
٣/٥ - (أ) - المعنى الذاتي للمصلحة والمفسدة :
فبالمعنى الذاتي تُفَسِّر المصلحة بالمنفعة، وتفسر المفسدة بالمضرة مطلقاً سواء أكان النفع أو الضرر شخصياً أو عاماً، غالباً أو مغلوباً، عاجلاً أو آجلاً إلخ.
فالعلم والربح واللذة والراحة والمتعة والصحة ونحوها كلها مصالح في ذاتها نافعة لأصحابها بأي طريق حصلت .
والجهل والخسارة والألم والتعب إلخ .. كلها مفاسد في ذاتها مضرة بأصحابها .
ولكن هذا النظر الذاتي في تحديد المصلحة والمفسدة هو نظر قاصر لا يكفي، ولا يصلح لبناء الأحكام الشرعية عليه :
- فإنَّ اللذة الوقتية مثلاً قد تعقب آلاماً أو مضار لصاحبها ولغيره في نفسه أو شرفه أو ماله كشرب المسكرات؛ وإن الراحة قد تعقب خساراً كبيراً وتعباً؛ وإنَّ الربح في بعض صوره أو طرقه قد يقوم على ظلم الغير أو على طرق غير شريفة لها ضرر أكبر من الربح.
-
وبالعكس قد نجد بعض الآلام أحسن نتيجة من عدمها، كآلام العلاج والمداواة ؛ وكذلك بعض المتاعب والمصاعب قد تتوقف عليها أطيب الثمرات. فالجهاد على ما فيه من ضرر بالأنفس والأموال تتوقف عليه حياة الأجيال الحاضرة والمستقبلة في الأمة وأمانها من خطر أعدائها.
لذلك وجب أن يُتَّخَذَ للمصالح والمفاسد التي يبنى عليها التشريع العام مقياس آخر غير المعنى الذاتي يعتبر به الشارع مصلحة الفرد
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. 1/5 - Al-Istislah is constructing legal rulings according to unrestricted interests (1). — Unrestricted interests are every interest for which no text exists in the Shari'ah specifying its consideration individually or by type. They are included in the general interests that manifest in attaining benefits and avoiding harms, those interests which Islamic law came to achieve in general, and its texts and principles indicate the necessity of observing them and taking them into account in organizing all aspects of life, and the Lawgiver did not specify individual instances, so they are called: mursalah, i.e., unrestricted, unspecified. If the interest is supported by a specific text, such as writing down the Qur'an to preserve it from loss and teaching reading and writing (2); or if it is of a type for which a general text testifies to its consideration, such as the obligation of teaching knowledge and spreading it in general, and the command of all kinds of good and the prohibition of all forms of evil, then it is among the textually indicated interests, individual or categorical, not unrestricted interests, and its ruling is considered established by that text, not by the rule of istislah. 2/5 - Clarification of the idea of interests and harms. To clarify the idea of unrestricted interests in Islam summarily, we say: benefit is the opposite of harm. Each of them is subject to consideration from two perspectives: from the perspective of the intrinsic meaning of benefit and harm. And from the perspective of their consideration in the view of the Lawgiver. 3/5 - (A) - The intrinsic meaning of benefit and harm: According to the intrinsic meaning, benefit is interpreted as advantage, and harm is interpreted as detriment absolutely, whether the benefit or harm is personal or general, predominant or outweighed, immediate or deferred, etc. Knowledge, profit, pleasure, comfort, enjoyment, health, and the like are all inherently beneficial to their owners in whatever way they are obtained. Ignorance, loss, pain, fatigue, etc., are all inherently harmful to their owners. But this intrinsic view of determining benefit and harm is deficient, insufficient, and not suitable for building legal rulings upon it: For temporary pleasure, for example, may be followed by pains or harms to its owner and others in his person, honor, or wealth, like drinking intoxicants; and comfort may be followed by great loss and fatigue; and profit in some of its forms or methods may be based on injustice to others or on dishonorable methods that have greater harm than the profit. Conversely, we may find some pains are better in result than their absence, like the pains of treatment and medication; and similarly, some troubles and difficulties may depend on the sweetest fruits. Jihad, despite its harm to lives and wealth, depends on the life of present and future generations of the nation and its security from the danger of its enemies. Therefore, it is necessary to adopt for the interests and harms upon which general legislation is built another criterion other than the intrinsic meaning, by which the Lawgiver considers the interest of the individual.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm introduces the concept of al-istislah (consideration of unrestricted interests) as a subsidiary source of Islamic fiqh. The author defines al-masalih al-mursalah as any interest not specifically or categorically indicated by a textual evidence. He distinguishes it from interests that have specific or general textual support, clarifying that when an interest is supported by a text, the ruling is based on that text, not on istislah. He then proceeds to clarify the ideas of maslaha (benefit) and mafsada (harm). He explains that each can be viewed from two angles: their intrinsic (subjective) meaning and their consideration in the Shari'ah. The intrinsic meaning defines maslaha as absolute benefit and mafsada as absolute harm. However, the author demonstrates the insufficiency of this subjective criterion through examples: temporary pleasures like alcohol lead to greater harms, while pains like medical treatment lead to greater benefits. He concludes that a different, Shari'ah-based criterion is necessary for legislation. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi approach to maslaha, which requires that any claimed benefit must be compatible with the general objectives of the Shari'ah and not contradict explicit texts.

Key Terms
الاستصلاح (al-istislah): Building legal rulings upon unrestricted interests (al-masalih al-mursalah)
المصالح المرسلة (al-masalih al-mursalah): Every interest for which no text (specific or general) has been revealed acknowledging it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what distinguishes an unrestricted interest (maslaha mursalah) from a textually indicated interest?
A) An unrestricted interest has a specific text mentioning it, while a textually indicated interest does not.
B) An unrestricted interest lacks any textual evidence, while a textually indicated interest has evidence either specific or general.
C) An unrestricted interest is always beneficial, while a textually indicated interest may be harmful.
D) An unrestricted interest is based on custom, while a textually indicated interest is based on the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Al-istislah is valid only for interests that have no textual recognition; if a text exists, the ruling comes from that text, not from istislah.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
The Intrinsic vs. Shar'i Concept of Maslaha and Mafsada
Critiquing the subjective definition of benefit and harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the subjective (intrinsic) meaning of maslaha and mafsada is insufficient for Islamic legislation and articulate the need for a Shar'i criterion based on the Lawgiver's perspective.

Core Idea
Subjective benefit is not enough: what seems beneficial may be harmful in the Shari'ah.

In this lesson, we explore the second part of the passage where the author critiques the 'intrinsic meaning' (al-ma'na al-dhati) of maslaha and mafsada. He shows through examples that pleasure, profit, and comfort can lead to harm, while pain and hardship can lead to benefit. This demonstrates that legal rulings cannot be based on subjective perceptions; instead, they must be derived from the Shari'ah's own criterion, which considers the overall good in light of texts and principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two perspectives
The passage says maslaha and mafsada can be viewed from two angles: the intrinsic meaning (subjective) and the Shari'ah's consideration. Focus on the first, which defines benefit as absolute advantage and harm as absolute detriment.
This subjective view is based on immediate human perception.
2
Analyze the examples of insufficiency
The author gives examples where subjective benefit is actually harmful (e.g., alcohol gives pleasure but causes harm) and subjective harm is actually beneficial (e.g., medical pain leads to health). Identify the contradiction in the subjective view.
Note that the examples involve both personal and social consequences.
3
Derive the conclusion
Because of these contradictions, a different criterion is needed—one that comes from the Shari'ah. The Lawgiver (Shari') determines what is truly beneficial or harmful for legislation.
This criterion is based on texts and maqasid, not on individual judgment.
4
Apply the Hanafi perspective
Hanafis hold that maslaha must be compatible with the maqasid al-shari'ah and not contradict any textual evidence. The intrinsic meaning is only a starting point; the Shari'ah may override it.
For example, the Hanafi school prohibits intoxicants despite their subjective pleasure.

Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh. 1/5 - Al-Istislah is constructing legal rulings according to unrestricted interests (1). — Unrestricted interests are every interest for which no text exists in the Shari'ah specifying its consideration individually or by type. They are included in the general interests that manifest in attaining benefits and avoiding harms, those interests which Islamic law came to achieve in general, and its texts and principles indicate the necessity of observing them and taking them into account in organizing all aspects of life, and the Lawgiver did not specify individual instances, so they are called: mursalah, i.e., unrestricted, unspecified. To clarify the idea of unrestricted interests in Islam summarily, we say: benefit is the opposite of harm. Each of them is subject to consideration from two perspectives: from the perspective of the intrinsic meaning of benefit and harm. And from the perspective of their consideration in the view of the Lawgiver. 3/5 - (A) - The intrinsic meaning of benefit and harm: According to the intrinsic meaning, benefit is interpreted as advantage, and harm is interpreted as detriment absolutely, whether the benefit or harm is personal or general, predominant or outweighed, immediate or deferred, etc. Knowledge, profit, pleasure, comfort, enjoyment, health, and the like are all inherently beneficial to their owners in whatever way they are obtained. Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-‘Amm introduces the concept of al-istislah (consideration of unrestricted interests) as a subsidiary source of Islamic fiqh. The author defines al-masalih al-mursalah as any interest not specifically or categorically indicated by a textual evidence. He distinguishes it from interests that have specific or general textual support, clarifying that when an interest is supported by a text, the ruling is based on that text, not on istislah. He then proceeds to clarify the ideas of maslaha (benefit) and mafsada (harm). He explains that each can be viewed from two angles: their intrinsic (subjective) meaning and their consideration in the Shari'ah. The intrinsic meaning defines maslaha as absolute benefit and mafsada as absolute harm. However, the author demonstrates the insufficiency of this subjective criterion through examples: temporary pleasures like alcohol lead to greater harms, while pains like medical treatment lead to greater benefits. He concludes that a different, Shari'ah-based criterion is necessary for legislation. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi approach to maslaha, which requires that any claimed benefit must be compatible with the general objectives of the Shari'ah and not contradict explicit texts.

Key Terms
المصلحة (al-maslaha): Benefit or advantage, interpreted subjectively as absolute benefit but requires Shar'i criterion for legislation
المفسدة (al-mafsada): Harm or detriment, interpreted subjectively as absolute harm but requires Shar'i criterion for prohibition
المعنى الذاتي (al-ma'na al-dhati): The intrinsic meaning of benefit/harm considered absolutely without regard to Shar'i evaluation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the intrinsic meaning of maslaha insufficient for building legal rulings?
A) Because it ignores the Shari'ah's consideration of long-term and broader consequences.
B) Because it is too complex to apply.
C) Because it only applies to individuals, not communities.
D) Because it contradicts the principle of istislah.

Key Takeaway
Islamic legislation requires a Shari'ah-based criterion for benefit and harm, not subjective perception.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
The Shar'i Criterion for Maslaha and Mafsada
Explaining why subjective utility is insufficient for Islamic legislation and establishing the shar'i criterion of maqasid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the shar'i consideration to evaluate whether a potential benefit qualifies as a valid maslaha for issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Subjective benefit is not enough; only benefits aligned with the Shari'ah's five essential pillars count as legitimate maslaha.

In this passage, Mustafa al-Zarqa explains the crucial distinction between subjective notions of benefit and harm and the Shari'ah's objective criteria. Understanding this is essential for any mufti, because a ruling based on mere apparent benefit may contradict the very purpose of Islamic law. The passage sets the foundation for how Hanafi jurists incorporate public interest within the framework of revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Subjective vs. Shar'i Maslaha
Identify the author's definition of subjective maslaha (any benefit) and subjective mafsada (any harm). Recognize that this view is deemed insufficient for legislation.
Consider examples: pleasure from intoxicants is subjectively beneficial, but shar'i considers it harmful.
2
Analyze the Critique of the Subjective Measure
Follow the author's reasoning: temporary pleasures may lead to greater harms, apparent pains (e.g., jihad) lead to greater goods. Understand why a shift is necessary.
This step prepares you to see the need for an objective criterion.
3
Identify the Shar'i Measure
Locate the author's statement that the true measure is the shar'i consideration (al-i'tibar al-shar'i), which evaluates maslaha and mafsada according to the objectives of the Shari'ah (maqasid).
The key phrase: 'ما اعتبره الشارع' – what the Lawgiver considers.
4
Recognize the Five Essential Pillars
Note that the foremost objectives are to safeguard religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property. Understand that these are universal and agreed upon by divine and positive laws.
These are called al-arkan al-khamsah or al-daruriyyat al-khams.
5
Understand the Classification of Masalih
The author mentions that scholars divide masalih into three categories: essentials (daruriyyat), needs (hajiyyat), and improvements (tahsiniyyat). The passage focuses on daruriyyat.
Only daruriyyat are detailed here; hajiyyat and tahsiniyyat are mentioned but not elaborated.

من جهة المعنى الذاتي للمصلحة والمفسدة. - ومن جهة اعتبارهما في نظر الشارع. ٣/٥ - (أ) - المعنى الذاتي للمصلحة والمفسدة : فبالمعنى الذاتي تُفَسِّر المصلحة بالمنفعة، وتفسر المفسدة بالمضرة مطلقاً سواء أكان النفع أو الضرر شخصياً أو عاماً، غالباً أو مغلوباً، عاجلاً أو آجلاً إلخ. فالعلم والربح واللذة والراحة والمتعة والصحة ونحوها كلها مصالح في ذاتها نافعة لأصحابها بأي طريق حصلت . والجهل والخسارة والألم والتعب إلخ .. كلها مفاسد في ذاتها مضرة بأصحابها . ولكن هذا النظر الذاتي في تحديد المصلحة والمفسدة هو نظر قاصر لا يكفي، ولا يصلح لبناء الأحكام الشرعية عليه : - فإنَّ اللذة الوقتية مثلاً قد تعقب آلاماً أو مضار لصاحبها ولغيره في نفسه أو شرفه أو ماله كشرب المسكرات؛ وإن الراحة قد تعقب خساراً كبيراً وتعباً؛ وإنَّ الربح في بعض صوره أو طرقه قد يقوم على ظلم الغير أو على طرق غير شريفة لها ضرر أكبر من الربح. - وبالعكس قد نجد بعض الآلام أحسن نتيجة من عدمها، كآلام العلاج والمداواة ؛ وكذلك بعض المتاعب والمصاعب قد تتوقف عليها أطيب الثمرات. فالجهاد على ما فيه من ضرر بالأنفس والأموال تتوقف عليه حياة الأجيال الحاضرة والمستقبلة في الأمة وأمانها من خطر أعدائها. لذلك وجب أن يُتَّخَذَ للمصالح والمفاسد التي يبنى عليها التشريع العام مقياس آخر غير المعنى الذاتي يعتبر به الشارع مصلحة الفرد والمجتمع معاً، ويوازن بين عاجل الحوائج وآجل النتائج، فلا يُعتبر عندئذ مصلحة أو مفسدة إلا ما اعتبره الشارع كذلك قطعاً لفوضى المقاييس الشخصية وتضاربها فتكون العبرة في ذلك إنما هي للاعتبار الشرعي. ٤/٥ - (ب) - الاعتبار الشرعي للمصلحة والمفسدة : إنَّ المصالح والمفاسد التي تعتبر مقياساً للأمر والنهي في الشرع الإسلامي هي التي تتفق أو تتنافى مع مقاصد الشريعة. وإن من أول مقاصدها صيانة الأركان الخمسة الضرورية للحياة البشرية وهي الدين . والنفس والعقل والنسل، والمال ؛ ثم ضمان ما سواها من الأمور التي تحتاج إليها الحياة الصالحة مما دون تلك الأركان الضرورية في أهميتها .. وتلك الأركان الخمسة قد اتفقت الشرائع الإلهية، بل والوضعية أيضاً، على وجوب احترامها وحفظها. وقد ذكر الغزالي في «المستصفى» أن [؟] ملة قط [؟] حرمتها لم تبح في [؟] وعلى هذا نرى أن علماء الفقه الإسلامي قسموا الأعمال والتصرفات التي تعد من المصالح بالنظر الشرعي، وبحسب دلائل نصوص الشريعة وأحكامها إلى ثلاثة أقسام : الأول الضروريات وهي الأعمال والتصرفات التي تتوقف عليها : صيانة الأركان الخمسة السالفة البيان. والنظر الشرعي أن هذه الأمور الخمسة لا بد منها للحياة الصالحة، فإذا فقد بعضها انهارت الحياة الإنسانية أو اختلت وفسَدَت. ولذا شرعت العبادات، وأبيح بل وجب الأكل والشرب واللبس بما يصون الأبدان ويستر السوات، كما نظمت أحكام المعاملات لصيانة الحقوق والأموال وشُرعَت العقوبات والتضمينات أي المسؤوليات المالية، زجراً عن العدوان وجَبْراً للحقوق. تقوم. فأساس الأعمال التي تعد من المصالح الضرورية أن لا الأمور الخمسة التي هي من أركان الحياة البشرية الصالحة إلا بمراعاتها . تلك
From the aspect of the subjective meaning of maslaha and mafsada. And from the aspect of their consideration in the view of the Lawgiver. 3/5 - (A) - The subjective meaning of maslaha and mafsada: By the subjective meaning, maslaha is interpreted as benefit, and mafsada is interpreted as harm absolutely, whether the benefit or harm is personal or general, predominant or overwhelmed, immediate or deferred, etc. So knowledge, profit, pleasure, comfort, enjoyment, health, and the like are all maslaha in themselves, beneficial to their owners by whatever means they are obtained. And ignorance, loss, pain, fatigue, etc. are all mafsada in themselves, harmful to their owners. But this subjective view in defining maslaha and mafsada is an insufficient view, not adequate, and not suitable for building legal rulings upon it: - For instance, temporary pleasure may be followed by pains or harms to its owner or others in his life, honor, or wealth, like drinking intoxicants; and comfort may be followed by great loss and fatigue; and profit in some of its forms or methods may be based on oppression of others or on dishonorable methods that have greater harm than the profit. - Conversely, we may find that some pains have a better result than their absence, like the pains of treatment and medication; and likewise, some troubles and hardships may have the sweetest fruits dependent upon them. For jihad, despite the harm it entails to lives and wealth, the life of present and future generations in the nation and their security from the danger of enemies depends upon it. Therefore, it was necessary that a measure other than the subjective meaning be adopted for the maslaha and mafsada upon which general legislation is built, by which the Lawgiver considers the maslaha of the individual and society together, and balances between immediate needs and deferred outcomes. So then, nothing is considered maslaha or mafsada except what the Lawgiver considers as such, to cut off the chaos and contradiction of personal measures. So the criterion in that is only the shar'i consideration. 4/5 - (B) - The shar'i consideration of maslaha and mafsada: Indeed, the masalih and mafasid that are considered a measure for command and prohibition in Islamic law are those that agree with or contradict the objectives of the Shari'ah. And among the foremost of its objectives is safeguarding the five essential pillars for human life: religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property; then securing besides them the matters that a good life needs, which are below those essential pillars in importance. And those five pillars have been agreed upon by divine laws, and even by positive laws, on the obligation of respecting and preserving them. And al-Ghazali mentioned in al-Mustasfa that [؟] never did [؟] permit their violation. And upon this, we see that the scholars of Islamic jurisprudence divided actions and transactions that are considered masalih by shar'i consideration, according to the evidence of the texts of Shari'ah and its rulings, into three categories: The first: the essentials (daruriyyat), which are actions and transactions upon which the safeguarding of the five aforementioned pillars depends. The shar'i consideration is that these five matters are indispensable for a good life; if some of them are missing, human life collapses or becomes disordered and corrupt. Hence, acts of worship were legislated, eating, drinking, and clothing to protect bodies and cover private parts were permitted (even obligatory), and the rulings of transactions were organized to safeguard rights and properties, and penalties and compensations (i.e., financial liabilities) were legislated to deter aggression and restore rights. So the basis of actions that are considered essential masalih is that the five matters which are pillars of good human life are not established except by observing them.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory section on the subsidiary sources of Islamic jurisprudence, specifically discussing the concept of istislah (consideration of public interest). The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, explains two key aspects: the subjective meaning of maslaha (benefit) and mafsada (harm), and the shar'i (legal) consideration of these concepts. He begins by defining maslaha subjectively as any benefit and mafsada as any harm, regardless of context. He then argues that this subjective view is insufficient for legislation because immediate benefits can lead to greater harms, and apparent harms can lead to greater benefits, as illustrated by examples like intoxicants and jihad. Therefore, a different measure is needed—the shar'i consideration, which evaluates maslaha and mafsada according to the objectives of the Shari'ah (maqasid al-shari'ah). The foremost of these objectives is the preservation of the five essential pillars: religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property. These are universal, agreed upon by divine and positive laws. Based on this, scholars classify acts into three categories: the essentials (daruriyyat), which are necessary for the preservation of these five pillars; the needs (hajiyyat); and the improvements (tahsiniyyat). The text elaborates on the daruriyyat, explaining that acts of worship, provisions for food and clothing, transactions, penalties, and financial compensations are all legislated to uphold these pillars. In the Hanafi school, this concept is foundational for understanding how maslaha is integrated within the framework of revealed texts (nusus) and qiyas (analogy), as the Hanafis do not accept independent maslaha (istislah) as a source but rather consider it within the scope of the texts and principles. This passage prepares the student to grasp how the Shari'ah balances individual and societal interests in legal rulings.

Key Terms
مصلحة (maslaha): Benefit or interest; in its subjective sense, any benefit to the individual, but in shar'i sense, only what aligns with the objectives of the Shari'ah.
مفسدة (mafsada): Harm or detriment; subjectively any harm, but shar'i mafsada is what opposes the objectives of the Shari'ah.
الاعتبار الشرعي (al-i'tibar al-shar'i): The legal consideration; the criterion by which the Shari'ah evaluates actions as beneficial or harmful based on its objectives, not subjective opinion.
الضروريات (al-daruriyyat): Essential matters; those actions and transactions necessary for the preservation of the five foundational pillars of human life.
الأركان الخمسة (al-arkan al-khamsah): The five essential pillars: religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property, which must be safeguarded for a good human life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary criterion for determining whether something is a maslaha (benefit) in Islamic legislation?
A) The subjective benefit to the individual, regardless of consequences.
B) The agreement of the majority of scholars.
C) Whether it aligns with the objectives of the Shari'ah, particularly the preservation of the five essential pillars.
D) Whether it brings immediate pleasure or profit.

Key Takeaway
The shar'i consideration, based on the five essential pillars, is the only valid criterion for determining maslaha in Islamic legislation.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

The Three Levels of Maslahah: Daruriyyat, Hajiyyat, Tahsiniyyat
Classification of public interests into three levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of the three levels of maslahah and provide a Shariah-based example for each.

Core Idea
The Shariah classifies public interests by necessity: essential (daruri), needful (haji), and embellishing (tahsini).

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of public interests (masalih) in Islamic law. Understanding these three levels—daruriyyat, hajiyyat, and tahsiniyyat—is essential for anyone seeking to apply the Shariah to real-life situations. The passage from al-Zarqa explains that the Shariah's objectives are built on preserving five essential pillars, and all rulings aim to serve interests at one of these three levels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five essential pillars
List the five pillars (religion, life, intellect, lineage, wealth) as the foundation of human good life.
These are called al-arkan al-khamsah and are universally agreed upon.
2
Define daruriyyat and give an example
Daruriyyat are actions upon which the preservation of the five pillars depends. Example: obligations like prayer (protects religion) and eating (protects life).
The text mentions acts of worship, eating/drinking, penalties, and financial laws.
3
Define hajiyyat and give an example
Hajiyyat are actions that remove hardship and provide ease, but their absence does not cause collapse. Example: contract of hire (ijarah) allows temporary use of property without ownership.
The text also gives hunting and enjoying good things as examples.
4
Define tahsiniyyat and give an example
Tahsiniyyat are matters of noble character and good custom; life is not distressed without them. Example: etiquette of eating, moderate spending.
These are also called takmiliyyat (completing matters).
5
Note the legislative hierarchy
The text states that rulings for essential pillars are most important, followed by needs, then embellishments. This hierarchy is key for conflict resolution.
Detailed conflict rule is covered in the next lesson.

٤/٥ - (ب) - الاعتبار الشرعي للمصلحة والمفسدة :
إنَّ المصالح والمفاسد التي تعتبر مقياساً للأمر والنهي في الشرع الإسلامي هي التي تتفق أو تتنافى مع مقاصد الشريعة. وإن من أول مقاصدها صيانة الأركان الخمسة الضرورية للحياة البشرية وهي الدين . والنفس والعقل والنسل، والمال ؛ ثم ضمان ما سواها من الأمور التي تحتاج إليها الحياة الصالحة مما دون تلك الأركان الضرورية في أهميتها .. وتلك الأركان الخمسة قد اتفقت الشرائع الإلهية، بل والوضعية أيضاً، على وجوب احترامها وحفظها. وقد ذكر الغزالي في «المستصفى» أن ملة قط . حرمتها لم تبح في وعلى هذا نرى أن علماء الفقه الإسلامي قسموا الأعمال والتصرفات التي تعد من المصالح بالنظر الشرعي، وبحسب دلائل نصوص الشريعة وأحكامها إلى ثلاثة أقسام :
الأول الضروريات وهي الأعمال والتصرفات التي تتوقف عليها :
صيانة الأركان الخمسة السالفة البيان. والنظر الشرعي أن هذه الأمور الخمسة لا بد منها للحياة الصالحة، فإذا فقد بعضها انهارت الحياة الإنسانية أو اختلت وفسَدَت.
ولذا شرعت العبادات، وأبيح بل وجب الأكل والشرب واللبس بما يصون الأبدان ويستر السوات، كما نظمت أحكام المعاملات لصيانة الحقوق والأموال وشُرعَت العقوبات والتضمينات أي المسؤوليات المالية، زجراً عن العدوان وجَبْراً للحقوق.
تقوم.
فأساس الأعمال التي تعد من المصالح الضرورية أن لا الأمور الخمسة التي هي من أركان الحياة البشرية الصالحة إلا بمراعاتها .
تلك
الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية الاستصلاح
الثاني: الحاجيات. وهي الأعمال والتصرّفات التي لا تتوقف عليها صيانة تلك الأركان الخمسة، ولكنها تتطلبها الحاجة لأجل التوسعة ورفع الحرج كإباحة الصيد والتمتع بالطيبات التي يمكن أن يستغني عنها الإنسان ولكن بشيء من المشقة؛ وكتشريع عقد الاستئجار وكثير من أنواع المعاملات .
ففتح طريق الاستئجار في المعاملات المدنية يحقق للناس وفاء حاجة كبرى، إذ يتمكن به كل منهم أن ينتفع بملك غيره لقاء عوض يسير بالنسبة إلى قيمة عين الشيء المأجور. ولو سُدَّ طريق الاستئجار لما تعطلت حياة الناس وما فسدت أوضاعهم، ولكن ينالهم حرج كبير : إذ يضطر الإنسان أن يملك عين ما يحتاج إليه ولو حاجة موقتة .
الثالث: التكميليات أو التحسينيات وهي التي لا تتحرج الحياة بتركها ولكن مراعاتها من مكارم الأخلاق أو من محاسن العادات، فهي من قبيل استكمال ما يليق والتنزه عما لا يليق، كآداب الكلام والطعام والشراب وكالاعتدال في المظاهر والاقتصاد في المصارف دون إسراف ولا تقتير ونحو ذلك.
وعلى هذا فالأحكام التي شرعت لصيانة الأركان الضرورية هي أهم الأحكام وأحقها بالمراعاة وتليها الأحكام المشروعة لضمان الحاجيات، ثم الأحكام المشروعة للتحسين والتكميل.
ولا يراعى حكم تحسيني إذا كان في مراعاته إخلال بما هو ضروري أو حاجي، لأن الفرع لا يراعى إذا كان في مراعاته والمحافظة عليه تفريط في الأصل ولذلك أبيح شرعاً كشف العورة عند الاقتضاء لأجل تشخيص داء، أو لمداواة أو عملية جراحية ضرورية، لأن ستر العورة من الأمور التحسينية التي غايتها أدبية ؛ أما العلاج فمن الضروريات لأن به صيانة النفس أو العقل أو النسل.
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh
...together with society, and balances immediate needs with future consequences. So at that point, nothing is considered a benefit or harm except what the Lawgiver considers as such, cutting off the chaos and conflict of personal standards. Thus the criterion in that is only the legislative consideration.
4/5 - (B) - The Legislative Consideration of Benefit and Harm:
Indeed, the benefits and harms that are considered a measure for command and prohibition in Islamic law are those that agree or conflict with the objectives of the Shariah. And among the first of its objectives is the preservation of the five essential pillars for human life, which are: religion, life, intellect, lineage, and wealth; then ensuring other matters that a good life needs, which are below those essential pillars in importance... And those five pillars have been agreed upon by divine laws, and even positive laws, as to the necessity of respecting and preserving them. Al-Ghazali mentioned in 'al-Mustasfa' that no religious community has permitted their violation. And upon this, we see that the scholars of Islamic Fiqh divided actions and transactions that are considered benefits according to legislative consideration, and according to the evidence of the texts of Shariah and its rulings, into three categories:
First: The Essentials (al-Daruriyyat): they are actions and transactions upon which depends the preservation of the five pillars mentioned above. The legislative view is that these five matters are indispensable for a good life; if any of them is missing, human life collapses or becomes disordered and corrupt.
Hence acts of worship were legislated, and eating, drinking, and clothing were permitted, indeed obligated, to preserve bodies and cover private parts; likewise, the rulings of transactions were organized to preserve rights and wealth, and punishments and financial liabilities (i.e., financial responsibilities) were legislated to deter aggression and compensate rights.
So the basis of actions that are considered essential benefits is that the five matters that are pillars of good human life cannot be established except by observing them.
Chapter (5): Subsidiary Sources: al-Istislah
Second: The Needs (al-Hajiyyat): they are actions and transactions upon which the preservation of those five pillars does not depend, but need requires them for expansion and removal of hardship, such as the permissibility of hunting and enjoying good things that a person could do without but with some hardship; and like the legislation of the contract of hire (ijarah) and many types of transactions.
Opening the way for hire in civil transactions fulfills a great need for people, as each can benefit from another's property in exchange for a small consideration relative to the value of the leased item itself. If the path of hire were blocked, people's lives would not be disrupted nor their conditions corrupted, but they would suffer great hardship: a person would be forced to own the very thing he needs, even if only temporarily.
Third: The Completing or Embellishing Matters (al-Takmiliyyat or al-Tahsiniyyat): they are those with whose abandonment life is not distressed, but observing them is part of noble morals or good customs. They are of the type of perfecting what is becoming and refraining from what is unbecoming, such as etiquettes of speech, food, and drink, and moderation in appearance and economy in spending without extravagance or miserliness, and the like.
Upon this, the rulings legislated to preserve the essential pillars are the most important rulings and most deserving of observance, followed by the rulings legislated to ensure needs, then the rulings legislated for embellishment and completion.
And an embellishing ruling is not observed if observing it violates something essential or needful, because the branch is not observed if observing and maintaining it causes neglect of the origin. For this reason, it is legally permissible to uncover the private parts when necessary for diagnosing a disease, or for treatment or essential surgery, because covering the private parts is an embellishing matter whose goal is etiquette; while treatment is from the essentials because it preserves life, intellect, or lineage.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's work discusses the classification of maslahah (public interest) in Islamic legal theory. After establishing that the Shariah's measure of benefit and harm is based on the objectives of the law (maqasid), the author explains that the primary objective is to preserve the five essential necessities (al-daruriyyat al-khams): religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property. The scholars divide actions considered beneficial into three categories: (1) Essentials (daruriyyat) — actions without which the five pillars cannot be maintained, such as worship, eating, clothing, transactional laws, and penalties. (2) Needs (hajiyyat) — actions that remove hardship and provide ease, like hunting, enjoying lawful pleasures, and the contract of hire (ijarah). The passage uses ijarah as a key example: it is not essential for survival but greatly eases transactions. (3) Embellishments (tahsiniyyat) — matters of ethics and good custom, such as proper manners in eating and spending moderately. The passage emphasizes a hierarchy: essential rulings take precedence over need-based rulings, and need-based over embellishments. A tahsini ruling is not observed if it conflicts with a daruri or haji ruling, illustrated by the example that uncovering the private parts (a tahsini matter normally prohibited) is permitted for medical treatment, which is daruri for preserving life or health. This prioritization is critical for fatwa; a mufti must weigh masalih according to this hierarchy.

Key Terms
الضروريات (al-daruriyyat): الأعمال والتصرفات التي تتوقف عليها صيانة الأركان الخمسة الضرورية للحياة البشرية
الحاجيات (al-hajiyyat): الأعمال التي لا تتوقف عليها صيانة الأركان الخمسة ولكنها مطلوبة للتوسعة ورفع الحرج.
التكميليات أو التحسينيات (al-tahsiniyyat): ما لا تتحرج الحياة بتركه ولكن مراعاته من مكارم الأخلاق.
الأركان الخمسة (al-arkan al-khamsah): العناصر الضرورية للحياة البشرية: الدين، النفس، العقل، النسل، المال.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a haji (need) according to the classification in the passage?
A) Obligation of prayer
B) Permissibility of hunting
C) Etiquette of eating
D) Preservation of religion

Key Takeaway
The Shariah divides masalih into three levels: essential (daruri), needful (haji), and embellishing (tahsini), with each level carrying different weight in legislation.

The Hierarchy of Masalih: Prioritization in Fatwa
Application of the hierarchy of masalih in a conflict scenario.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a lower-level interest is not observed if it conflicts with a higher-level interest, using the example of medical treatment overriding the rule of covering private parts.

Core Idea
A tahsini (embellishing) ruling is abandoned if it conflicts with a daruri (essential) or haji (need) ruling, because the branch cannot override the root.

While the previous lesson defined the three levels of maslahah, this lesson focuses on the crucial rule that governs their interaction: the hierarchy of precedence. Understanding that a tahsini ruling cannot be upheld if it violates a daruri or haji ruling is vital for muftis who must resolve conflicts between divine directives in real-world situations.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three levels of maslahah
Review the order: daruri (essential), haji (need), tahsini (embellishment).
This order is established in the previous lesson.
2
State the hierarchical principle
The passage states: 'ولا يراعى حكم تحسيني إذا كان في مراعاته إخلال بما هو ضروري أو حاجي' and adds 'الفرع لا يراعى إذا كان في مراعاته والمحافظة عليه تفريط في الأصل'.
The principle: a lower-level ruling (branch) is not observed if it causes neglect of a higher-level ruling (origin).
3
Apply to the medical example
Identify the conflict: covering private parts (tahsini) vs. medical treatment (daruri for life/intellect/lineage). Since daruri > tahsini, the tahsini ruling is waived.
The passage explicitly gives this example.
4
Conclude the fatwa implication
A mufti must always check whether observing a lower-level interest would harm a higher one. If so, the higher interest prevails.
This is a core tool for resolving apparent conflicts between Shariah rulings.

الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
والمجتمع معاً، ويوازن بين عاجل الحوائج وآجل النتائج، فلا يُعتبر عندئذ مصلحة أو مفسدة إلا ما اعتبره الشارع كذلك قطعاً لفوضى المقاييس الشخصية وتضاربها فتكون العبرة في ذلك إنما هي للاعتبار الشرعي.
٤/٥ - (ب) - الاعتبار الشرعي للمصلحة والمفسدة :
إنَّ المصالح والمفاسد التي تعتبر مقياساً للأمر والنهي في الشرع الإسلامي هي التي تتفق أو تتنافى مع مقاصد الشريعة. وإن من أول مقاصدها صيانة الأركان الخمسة الضرورية للحياة البشرية وهي الدين . والنفس والعقل والنسل، والمال ؛ ثم ضمان ما سواها من الأمور التي تحتاج إليها الحياة الصالحة مما دون تلك الأركان الضرورية في أهميتها .. وتلك الأركان الخمسة قد اتفقت الشرائع الإلهية، بل والوضعية أيضاً، على وجوب احترامها وحفظها. وقد ذكر الغزالي في «المستصفى» أن ملة قط . حرمتها لم تبح في وعلى هذا نرى أن علماء الفقه الإسلامي قسموا الأعمال والتصرفات التي تعد من المصالح بالنظر الشرعي، وبحسب دلائل نصوص الشريعة وأحكامها إلى ثلاثة أقسام :
الأول الضروريات وهي الأعمال والتصرفات التي تتوقف عليها :
صيانة الأركان الخمسة السالفة البيان. والنظر الشرعي أن هذه الأمور الخمسة لا بد منها للحياة الصالحة، فإذا فقد بعضها انهارت الحياة الإنسانية أو اختلت وفسَدَت.
ولذا شرعت العبادات، وأبيح بل وجب الأكل والشرب واللبس بما يصون الأبدان ويستر السوات، كما نظمت أحكام المعاملات لصيانة الحقوق والأموال وشُرعَت العقوبات والتضمينات أي المسؤوليات المالية، زجراً عن العدوان وجَبْراً للحقوق.
تقوم.
فأساس الأعمال التي تعد من المصالح الضرورية أن لا الأمور الخمسة التي هي من أركان الحياة البشرية الصالحة إلا بمراعاتها .
تلك
الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية الاستصلاح
الثاني: الحاجيات. وهي الأعمال والتصرّفات التي لا تتوقف عليها صيانة تلك الأركان الخمسة، ولكنها تتطلبها الحاجة لأجل التوسعة ورفع الحرج كإباحة الصيد والتمتع بالطيبات التي يمكن أن يستغني عنها الإنسان ولكن بشيء من المشقة؛ وكتشريع عقد الاستئجار وكثير من أنواع المعاملات .
ففتح طريق الاستئجار في المعاملات المدنية يحقق للناس وفاء حاجة كبرى، إذ يتمكن به كل منهم أن ينتفع بملك غيره لقاء عوض يسير بالنسبة إلى قيمة عين الشيء المأجور. ولو سُدَّ طريق الاستئجار لما تعطلت حياة الناس وما فسدت أوضاعهم، ولكن ينالهم حرج كبير : إذ يضطر الإنسان أن يملك عين ما يحتاج إليه ولو حاجة موقتة .
الثالث: التكميليات أو التحسينيات وهي التي لا تتحرج الحياة بتركها ولكن مراعاتها من مكارم الأخلاق أو من محاسن العادات، فهي من قبيل استكمال ما يليق والتنزه عما لا يليق، كآداب الكلام والطعام والشراب وكالاعتدال في المظاهر والاقتصاد في المصارف دون إسراف ولا تقتير ونحو ذلك.
وعلى هذا فالأحكام التي شرعت لصيانة الأركان الضرورية هي أهم الأحكام وأحقها بالمراعاة وتليها الأحكام المشروعة لضمان الحاجيات، ثم الأحكام المشروعة للتحسين والتكميل.
ولا يراعى حكم تحسيني إذا كان في مراعاته إخلال بما هو ضروري أو حاجي، لأن الفرع لا يراعى إذا كان في مراعاته والمحافظة عليه تفريط في الأصل ولذلك أبيح شرعاً كشف العورة عند الاقتضاء لأجل تشخيص داء، أو لمداواة أو عملية جراحية ضرورية، لأن ستر العورة من الأمور التحسينية التي غايتها أدبية ؛ أما العلاج فمن الضروريات لأن به صيانة النفس أو العقل أو النسل.
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Fiqh
...together with society, and balances immediate needs with future consequences. So at that point, nothing is considered a benefit or harm except what the Lawgiver considers as such, cutting off the chaos and conflict of personal standards. Thus the criterion in that is only the legislative consideration.
4/5 - (B) - The Legislative Consideration of Benefit and Harm:
Indeed, the benefits and harms that are considered a measure for command and prohibition in Islamic law are those that agree or conflict with the objectives of the Shariah. And among the first of its objectives is the preservation of the five essential pillars for human life, which are: religion, life, intellect, lineage, and wealth; then ensuring other matters that a good life needs, which are below those essential pillars in importance... And those five pillars have been agreed upon by divine laws, and even positive laws, as to the necessity of respecting and preserving them. Al-Ghazali mentioned in 'al-Mustasfa' that no religious community has permitted their violation. And upon this, we see that the scholars of Islamic Fiqh divided actions and transactions that are considered benefits according to legislative consideration, and according to the evidence of the texts of Shariah and its rulings, into three categories:
First: The Essentials (al-Daruriyyat): they are actions and transactions upon which depends the preservation of the five pillars mentioned above. The legislative view is that these five matters are indispensable for a good life; if any of them is missing, human life collapses or becomes disordered and corrupt.
Hence acts of worship were legislated, and eating, drinking, and clothing were permitted, indeed obligated, to preserve bodies and cover private parts; likewise, the rulings of transactions were organized to preserve rights and wealth, and punishments and financial liabilities (i.e., financial responsibilities) were legislated to deter aggression and compensate rights.
So the basis of actions that are considered essential benefits is that the five matters that are pillars of good human life cannot be established except by observing them.
Chapter (5): Subsidiary Sources: al-Istislah
Second: The Needs (al-Hajiyyat): they are actions and transactions upon which the preservation of those five pillars does not depend, but need requires them for expansion and removal of hardship, such as the permissibility of hunting and enjoying good things that a person could do without but with some hardship; and like the legislation of the contract of hire (ijarah) and many types of transactions.
Opening the way for hire in civil transactions fulfills a great need for people, as each can benefit from another's property in exchange for a small consideration relative to the value of the leased item itself. If the path of hire were blocked, people's lives would not be disrupted nor their conditions corrupted, but they would suffer great hardship: a person would be forced to own the very thing he needs, even if only temporarily.
Third: The Completing or Embellishing Matters (al-Takmiliyyat or al-Tahsiniyyat): they are those with whose abandonment life is not distressed, but observing them is part of noble morals or good customs. They are of the type of perfecting what is becoming and refraining from what is unbecoming, such as etiquettes of speech, food, and drink, and moderation in appearance and economy in spending without extravagance or miserliness, and the like.
Upon this, the rulings legislated to preserve the essential pillars are the most important rulings and most deserving of observance, followed by the rulings legislated to ensure needs, then the rulings legislated for embellishment and completion.
And an embellishing ruling is not observed if observing it violates something essential or needful, because the branch is not observed if observing and maintaining it causes neglect of the origin. For this reason, it is legally permissible to uncover the private parts when necessary for diagnosing a disease, or for treatment or essential surgery, because covering the private parts is an embellishing matter whose goal is etiquette; while treatment is from the essentials because it preserves life, intellect, or lineage.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's work discusses the classification of maslahah (public interest) in Islamic legal theory. After establishing that the Shariah's measure of benefit and harm is based on the objectives of the law (maqasid), the author explains that the primary objective is to preserve the five essential necessities (al-daruriyyat al-khams): religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property. The scholars divide actions considered beneficial into three categories: (1) Essentials (daruriyyat) — actions without which the five pillars cannot be maintained, such as worship, eating, clothing, transactional laws, and penalties. (2) Needs (hajiyyat) — actions that remove hardship and provide ease, like hunting, enjoying lawful pleasures, and the contract of hire (ijarah). The passage uses ijarah as a key example: it is not essential for survival but greatly eases transactions. (3) Embellishments (tahsiniyyat) — matters of ethics and good custom, such as proper manners in eating and spending moderately. The passage emphasizes a hierarchy: essential rulings take precedence over need-based rulings, and need-based over embellishments. A tahsini ruling is not observed if it conflicts with a daruri or haji ruling, illustrated by the example that uncovering the private parts (a tahsini matter normally prohibited) is permitted for medical treatment, which is daruri for preserving life or health. This prioritization is critical for fatwa; a mufti must weigh masalih according to this hierarchy.

Key Terms
الضروريات (al-daruriyyat): الأعمال والتصرفات التي تتوقف عليها صيانة الأركان الخمسة الضرورية للحياة البشرية
الحاجيات (al-hajiyyat): الأعمال التي لا تتوقف عليها صيانة الأركان الخمسة ولكنها مطلوبة للتوسعة ورفع الحرج.
التكميليات أو التحسينيات (al-tahsiniyyat): ما لا تتحرج الحياة بتركه ولكن مراعاته من مكارم الأخلاق.
الفرع (al-far'): الحكم الأقل أهمية في التدرج (كالتحسيني) بالنسبة إلى الأصل الضروري أو الحاجي.
الأصل (al-asl): الحكم الأعلى أهمية في التدرج (كالضروري أو الحاجي).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy of masalih, why is it permissible to uncover the private parts for surgery?
A) Because covering is not obligatory.
B) Because treatment is a daruri that overrides the tahsini rule of covering.
C) Because both are haji.
D) Because the surgery is tahsini.

Key Takeaway
When a tahsini ruling conflicts with a daruri or haji ruling, the higher level prevails, and the lower level is waived.
